when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師 , 她確實做了一些 , 但真正重要的是要說未來會遠遠超過這個 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這傢伙來了艾倫•圖靈在1936年重創了電腦
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械化的
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論上的
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩位都是來自數學的觀點 , 但turing告訴我們非常重要的一點 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他奠定了計算機科學的數學基礎 , 然後說: 「 不論你怎麼製造電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你的電腦是不是像babbage那樣是機械的 , 或者像今天的電子 , 又或者是未來的電腦 , 細胞 , 又或者 , 再次的 , 機械的 , 一旦我們進入了奈米技術
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器把它做得很小 。 所有這些東西都是電腦
there is in a sense a computing essence .	有一種運算本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這稱為 「 教堂論 」 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你有了個聯繫 , 你說巴貝奇設計的這個東西真的是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它有能力用電腦來做所有我們現在做的事 , 只是速度真的很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	讓大家知道有多慢 , 大約1k的記憶體有多慢 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它使用打孔卡 , 也就是進食 , 它的速度比第一台zx81要慢一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它確實有一個ram包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以增加大量的記憶力 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天這又把我們帶到哪裡 ?
so there are plans .	所以有了計劃 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在swindon科學博物館的檔案中有上百個計劃和上千頁文章是charlesbabbage寫的關於這個分析引擎的筆記
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中有一套計畫叫作 「 計劃28 」 , 這也是我和doronswade所創立的一個慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的管理者 , 也是開動這個計劃的人 , 來建造一個不同的引擎 , 我們的計劃就是要把它做出來 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計畫有好幾部分要處理 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其一是掃描babbage的檔案
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	已經完成了 。 第二個是研究所有計劃中的一項 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是模擬那台機器的電腦 , 最後一部分是在科學博物館建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它完成時 , 你將終於能夠理解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為與其在你面前擁有一個微小的晶片 , 你必須看著這個巨大的東西然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作 , cpu在運作 , 我聽見它在運作 。 我大概聞到了它的味道 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但是在這之間我們要做一個模擬
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫的 , 他說 , 當分析引擎存在的時候 , 它一定會引導未來的科學發展 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有成功過 , 因為他總是在想新的計劃 , 但是當它真的在1940年代被建造時 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我讓各位稍微體驗一下它在動作的樣子 , 這段影片顯示出局部的cpu運作機制 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以這只是三組齒輪它還會加上 。 這是加法的運作原理所以你想像這個巨大的機器
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年時間
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代以前 , 我們會有
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這場影像填滿了艾倫•阿修斯伯特蘭近期的演說 , 他的三項計畫 , 包括人性和棲息地 , 驚人的空拍照片 , 用他的 「 來自地球 」 的節目 , 來自全球各地的個人訪談 , 在他的網路專案 「 六十億人 」 中展現出來 , 他很快就推出了 「 家 」 , 這部電影紀錄了人類透過電子呼吸拍攝來產生的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人類、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	伊恩•阿姆斯伯特用廣角度捕捉地球是很脆弱的
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 可以靠飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸的二氧化碳 , 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡是為了談談生態 , 我在一年內排放的二氧化碳量和法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	那我該怎麼辦 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	我在家裡回來時 , 得殺一位法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來抵銷我的碳 , 就像我每次都這樣做 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的作品是要展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子一些我去年拍攝的最後一張照片 。

in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省 , 人們不停工作 , 24小時7小時 , 盡可能的抽取石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的終點
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙不是長期的解決方法
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油量是發現的三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不願相信我們所知道的
coral reef in new caledonia .	新克里多尼亞州的珊瑚礁
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	一百分之百的珊瑚可能在2050年前就因全球暖化而消失了 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 而且對海洋的生物多樣性也非常重要 。

we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都對地球的禮物有著同樣的需求 , 希望能超越我們自己 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們卻仍舊繼續築起圍牆 , 保持距離 。

we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在危害自己 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的這場演說中 , 理查德•瑞斯尼克顯示了將來健康照護顛倒是多麼便宜 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、醫療保健、科學、技術、
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	richardresnick:歡迎來到基因革命
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我給各位看人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方的是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女人有兩份大的x染色體 ; 男人有x染色體 , 當然 , 還有那個小的y染色體 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	很抱歉男孩 , 但這只是讓你與眾不同之處的一個小東西 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	如果你放大這個基因組的圖片 , 那你會看到這個雙螺旋結構--生命的編碼有這四個生化字母 , 我們稱之為基對:a , c , g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是一個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以隨便丟出大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把這1280像素的每一個像素上都安置一個基對 , 到800個解析度的螢幕上 , 我們就需要3000個螢幕來檢視基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 順便一提 , 有一群y染色體的人 , 決定想要將它排序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	實際上 , 15年後 , 約40億美元的資金 , 基因組被定序並發表了 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最後的版本發表 , 他們繼續致力於
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是在這樣的一台機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每個鹼基的成本大約是1美元 , 是一種非常慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我在此告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在我們將一個基因組複製50份然後將這些複製品切成50基對接著我們將它們進行大量平行排序
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把這套軟體融入其中 , 重新組合然後告訴大家故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	給大家看看這看起來像什麼 , 人類基因組計畫:3gabs , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	每週可以運行200gabass
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	而今年夏天 , 200將會改變到6000個 , 這速度下並沒有減慢的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以一個基對排序的價格已經下跌了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這等於是你在1998年給汽車加滿一次油的錢 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開到木星 , 開兩次回到木星 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc地點、所有醫療文獻的檔案 , 摩爾定律 , 過去的排序方法 , 這裡都是新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是對數刻度 , 你們通常不會看到那樣的上升線 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	全世界用於人類基因組測序的能力大約在今年五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們是根據被放置的機器知道的 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預計在可預見的未來中 , 每年都會增加一倍、三倍或四倍 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個實驗室 , 代表了20%的能力 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人絕對是贏了這場比賽來到新月球順帶一提
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有何意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以一個女人到了37歲
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她呈現的就是第二期雌激素受體陽性乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受了手術 , 化療和放射治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後她又回來了 「 階段三c卵巢癌 」
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次接受手術和化療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後她42歲 , 罹患了更多的卵巢癌 , 更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她回來時患上了急性髓性白血病 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 並在八天後過世 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位女性被對待的方式 , 不到十年 , 就會看起來像在流血 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	而是因為有像我同事rickwilson在華盛頓大學基因研究所的人們決定要看一下這個女生的後遺症
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	然後他做定序 , 取出皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 癌骨髓 , 然後他為兩者做完整的基因組排序 , 幾週後 , 都沒有大成本 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他在軟體中比較這兩組基因他發現在其他事物中就是一個刪除一個2 , 000個鹼基對在一個叫做tp53的基因上
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你的這種基因中發生了破壞性的突變 , 你一生中有90%的可能性會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對這位女性並沒有幫助 , 但這對她家人的確有嚴重、深刻的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 若他們有相同的突變 , 且他們會得到這基因測試 , 且他們了解它 , 那麼他們就能去做定期的篩檢 , 且能及早偵測到癌症 , 且有可能過更長壽 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	現在讓我來介紹啤酒雙胞胎 , 在兩歲的時候被診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是一位非常勇敢的女性 , 她不相信那些病症並不一致 , 通過一些英勇的努力和大量的網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 實際上他們有些什麼別的 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所患的是具有分裂性的肌張力不全症
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	因此 , 他們給了左旋多巴 , 他們的症狀確實會改善 , 但並沒有完全消除症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	照片裡的這位先生是joebeery男士 , 幸運的是他在一家叫做生命科技公司的公司擔任執行長 。

and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他的做法是讓他的孩子做定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現一個叫做spr的基因有一系列變異這個基因負責產生血清素和其他東西
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以在左旋多巴上 , 他們給這些孩子一種血清素的前兆藥物 , 現在他們很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 如果沒有全基因組測序 , 這種情形就永遠不會發生 。

so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有個小nick喜歡蝙蝠俠和水槍 。

and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	不是說他沒有吃東西 , 而是他吃東西的時候 , 他的腸道基本上打開了 , 排泄物溢出到他的腸道 。

and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	它們會發現 , 一個可控制細胞死亡的基因突變 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以理論是說 , 他對發生在食物中的非正常反應基本上 , 這是自然的反應 , 這反應引起某些細胞的死亡 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾•克拉夫特展示他的骨髓採取一種新裝置 , 它能迅速地收集救命的骨髓 , 用最少的疼痛對付捐贈者 。 他強調 , 在骨髓中找到的成體幹細胞 , 可以被用來治療許多臨終疾病 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟疾病 。

and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓 , 則是我們用來拯救數萬名病人的生命 , 大部分的病人都患有先進的惡性腫瘤 , 例如白血病和淋巴瘤 , 以及其他一些疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛做移植研究 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術房裡 。 我們有鮑勃在這裡 , 他是義工捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們將他的骨髓傳遍全國 , 以拯救白血病孩童的性命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何採收這塊骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 麻醉醫師 , 護士 , 以及另一位醫生 , 來自我旁邊 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob躺在桌上 , 然後我們把這個小針筒 , 你知道 , 不要太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們的做法是將它放置在軟組織中 , 將它刺入硬的骨頭 , 進入tuchus這個術語 , 每次用針筒將大約10mls的骨髓移出 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把針筒傳給護士 , 她把針筒放進一個針筒裡
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	交回給我 。 我們一而再 , 再而三地這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	大約兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	到最後 , 我的手臂酸痛 , 我手上有一台呼叫器 , 更不用說bob了 , 他的屁股看起來更像這個樣子 , 像個瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個程序在大約40年後都沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能有更好的方式可以做 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到了一個微創傷的方法 , 和一個我們稱為 「 骨髓採取器 」 的新儀器 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而這個骨髓採取器 , 它的運作方式如下 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準看診病人
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	我們不但進入了數十次的骨頭 , 反而進入了剛才的臀部或後面的骨頭 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個很靈活、有力的導管 , 有一個特別的導管管 , 它會停留在骨髓的脆弱部分 , 跟著臀部的輪廓 , 隨著它四處移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它會讓你非常快速的渴望 , 或吸乾 , 豐富的骨髓快速地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以在同一個入口上多次通過 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	很快地 , 鮑勃就能買到一個穿刺 , 局部麻醉 , 做為門診病人的收穫 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 , 在史丹佛得到了一個小額資助 。
and played around with this a little bit .	稍微玩一下 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們團隊的成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們有了兩項大型動物和豬的研究
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們驚奇地發現 , 我們不僅僅是從骨髓中取出骨髓 , 還從骨髓採取器中取出了10倍的幹細胞活動 , 相對於正常的設備 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這裝置在去年剛剛被美國食品及藥物管理局批准
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是一位活體病人 。 你可以看到它跟隨四周的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人 , 同一個洞裡 , 會有兩條通過 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是局部麻醉劑 , 作為門診病人 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	我們得到的幹細胞數目是同一個病人的標準做法的三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	那為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是非常豐富的成體幹細胞來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	各位都知道胚胎幹細胞
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力但尚未進入臨床試驗階段
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成體幹細胞遍佈我們的全身 , 包括我們骨髓中血液循環的幹細胞 , 這種我們已經用它作為幹細胞療法的一種形式 , 用了超過四十年的時間 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	近十年來 , 骨髓幹細胞大量使用 , 用來治療病人其它疾病 , 如心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程、甚至神經學 , 來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	今年 , 我們剛剛站出來 , 正在商業化--2.0的骨髓採取者 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望能將更多幹細胞取出 , 轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人登記成為能拯救生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你在年輕及健康的時期 , 儲存你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 未來還能使用它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後--這是我們骨髓移植手術的照片 , 他們每年都會在史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來能有更多這樣的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪家葛瑞特•萊西提出一個有爭議的宇宙的新模型可能可以解答所有大哉問 。 如果沒有其他的 , 它就是最漂亮的8d模型 , 最漂亮的8d8d模型 , 由你所見過的基本粒子和力所組成 。
physics , science , technology	物理 , 科學 , 科技
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garretlisi理論上的每一件事
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看那些可殺的方程式 。 甜心 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	其實 , 在接下來的18分鐘裡我要盡可能不用方程式來描述粒子物理的美
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	發現有很多我們可以從珊瑚身上學到的東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是種非常美麗且不尋常的動物
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一個珊瑚群都由成千上萬的珊瑚組成 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚會持續侵蝕和分枝成為基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這些珊瑚可以是超級聰明的珊瑚 , 我們可以分離出一個個體 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問 , 他在這個特別的地點與他的鄰居相比 , 是不是只是偶然 , 命運 , 還是什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們招募溫度太高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全是愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以很像 , 你看 , 我有衝浪的疤痕 , 可以證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這珊瑚會持續跟我們說他的鄰居對他的複製性是一模一樣的 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在所有其他地點 , 以獨特的個體來體驗 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚來說分支成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同的是 , 超級智慧的珊瑚有獨特的準備來了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述了我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是持續地擴展到不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 這是很奇怪的事情 , 因為我們只能經歷一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子詭異的現象最早是由薛丁格和他的貓來描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓更喜歡這個版本
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個環境中 , 薛丁格待在一個具有放射物質的箱子中 , 透過量子力學定律 , 將量子力學的分支帶入一個放射量子力學的狀態 , 一個放射性物質的狀態 , 而它並不是的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在樣本散發出的分支中 , 它會啟動扳機 , 釋放毒氣 , 薛丁格也死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支 , 他還是活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每個人分別經歷這些現實 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	相反的 , 另一隻也不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為我們每個人都只會體驗到個別的存在 , 且我們沒辦法看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像我們每一個人 , 像薛丁格這裡的 " 薛丁格 " 一樣 , 是一種珊瑚分支到不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這就是微小世界的運作方式 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以用一句話來總結:所有可能發生的一切 , 都可以 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示每件事都會發生
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其他的物理則是描述哪些可能發生 , 哪些不行 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們一切都可用幾何學以及基本粒子的相互作用
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些互動是完全平衡的情況下 , 事情才能發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我將描述我們對這些粒子的認識它們是什麼以及它的平衡機制如何運作
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這台機器中 , 質子和反質子的光束會被加速到接近光速的速度 , 並在對撞中聚集 , 產生出一股巨大的純能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這些能量立刻被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴射流 , 探測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這個巨大的機器 , 大型強子對撞機在日內瓦的歐洲核子研究中心有個圓周長有17英哩在營運中 , 比蒙特雷全市用電量多了五倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法明確預測在任何一次對撞中會產生哪些粒子 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能的實現
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們哪些粒子可能產生
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量必定與質子和反質子相同
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能量極限更大的粒子都沒有產生 , 對我們而言還是隱形的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這種新型粒子加速器那麼令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將超越過去所做過的七倍能量極限 , 所以我們很快就會看到新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談到我們可能看到的現象之前 , 讓我先描述一下我們已知的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一整個亞原子粒子的動物園
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都很熟悉電子
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在座的很多人都在過得很好的生活 , 把他們推來推去 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子有個中性的夥伴叫做中子 , 沒有電荷和極小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 由上到下的夸克有著非常大的質量 , 結合成三 , 就能製造原子中子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子分成左旋和右旋它們都有攜帶相反電荷的反粒子
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子還有我們不太熟悉的第二代和第三代擁有與第一代相同的載荷但有更高的質量
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些粒子都和各種力子互相作用
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過光子傳遞質子相互作用
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常微弱的力學叫做 , 超乎想像的弱力 , 只和左撇子的物質發生交互作用
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用 , 帶有不同的載荷 , 叫做 「 色荷 」 , 分別為三種不同種:紅、綠、藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygell-mann這些名字-這是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後是重力是重力藉由質量與旋轉與物質相互作用
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是每一種力都對應有不同的載荷
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種力通過各自粒子所對應的載荷相互作用
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看見的粒子但我們很確定的存在希格斯粒子也就是希格斯粒子讓其他粒子有了質量
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是看到希格斯粒子而我們幾乎可以肯定它會
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的奧秘是我們還能看到什麼 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我將向你們展示這個演講的結尾漂亮的可能性 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	如果我們用不同的自旋和載荷計算所有這些不同的粒子共有226種
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	也就是有很多的粒子要持續追蹤
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然擁有這麼多的基本粒子是很奇怪的 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據它們的載荷把它們畫出來 , 一些美麗的圖案就會浮現出來 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子擁有一個負電荷而夸克擁有1/3的電荷
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以 , 當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克生成質子時 , 加上一顆上子就會有全電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子還有反粒子它們具有相反的載荷
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷實際上是兩種載荷的結合超荷和弱荷
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開在這個二度載荷空間中畫出粒子的載荷電荷就在這些粒子的垂直方向上
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力通過超荷和弱荷與物質相互作用而形成這個圖案
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這被稱作電弱統一模型 , 早在1967年就已經完成了 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	大部份人只熟悉電荷而非兩者都是因為希格斯粒子
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子質量很大破壞了電弱型式的對稱性
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	通過給弱子較大的質量使弱力更加微弱
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於大量的希格斯粒子在水平方向排列 , 電磁力的光子仍然不大質量 , 並在載荷空間中與電荷相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力在二度空間中被粒子載荷的型式所描述
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力的部份加進去 , 做法是將它的兩個載荷方向分開 , 把載荷用夸克形式沿這些方向畫出來 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度載荷空間中畫出來然後投影到二度空間這樣我們就可以看見
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	只要粒子相互作用大自然會在四個載荷方向上保持完美的平衡
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果一個粒子和一個反粒子相撞會產生能量四個電荷方向的載荷疊加變為零
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時 , 任何東西都可以被創造出來 , 只要它有相同的能量 , 並能保持一個完全負荷的零 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如說這個弱子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的相互作用中載荷必須保持平衡
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	一個弱子可以衰退成一個電子和一個反中微子而這三個粒子仍然是零荷
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些電荷的型式不僅漂亮
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	告訴我們什麼樣的互動是可以實現的
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉這個載荷空間 , 以便更好地觀察到強相互作用 , 這有一個不錯的六角形結構 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強相互作用中強子比如說這個會和有色夸克相互作用比如這個綠色1 , 給一個夸克一個不一樣的色荷這個紅夸克
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強相互作用每秒鐘會發生幾百萬次 , 在我們身體的每個原子中 , 讓原子核靠在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但三種力相對應的這四種載荷還不是終點
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以多包含兩個載荷對應到重力的作用
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	納入這些 , 每個粒子會有兩種不同的旋轉載荷 , 自旋向上和自旋向下 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間中給一個不錯的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個圖案 , 看到它相當漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	此時此刻 , 這種圖案符合我們目前所知 , 大自然如何在這些基本粒子的尺度下建立 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們能確定的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	其中的一些粒子在實驗中是我們能到達的極限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式 , 我們已經知道這些微小尺度的粒子物理學 。 宇宙如何以這些微小的尺度運作 , 是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要來談談我們還不知道的事物一些新古老的想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要把這個模式單獨用數學來拓展看看我們能否把我們的手延伸到整個enchilada
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們希望找到構成我們宇宙的所有粒子和力量
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張圖來預測新的粒子我們會看到何時實驗到達更高能量
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	在粒子物理學中有一個古老的想法 , 就是這種已知的載荷模式 , 這種不對稱的形態 , 可以從一個更完美的圖案中浮現出來 , 類似希格斯粒子如何突破電弱圖案來產生電磁力 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了要做到這一點 , 我們需要引入具有新的載荷方向的新力 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們導入一個新方向時 , 我們要猜測粒子在這個方向上帶什麼樣的載荷 , 然後我們就能讓它跟其他粒子一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們猜得更明智 , 就能把標準載荷構建在六度載荷空間中 , 當作是七度載荷空間中這個更完美的圖案的對稱性 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這種特殊的選擇 , 與1973年帕提和薩拉姆提出的大統一理論相對應 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看到這個新的統一模式 , 我們可以看到一些空隙 , 粒子似乎缺少了些什麼 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的研究方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家在尋找更大、更對稱的模式 , 包括已建立的模式 , 作為一個子集 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測那些從未被看見的粒子的存在
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 它應該和弱力很像 , 只會比較弱 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這組載荷集 , 並考慮到一個奇怪的事實:在六度載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代擁有和第一代物質擁有完全相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不是靠它們的六個載荷來辨別的 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在彼此的標準載荷空間上 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那我們就能對每一個粒子施加獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個圖案是什麼樣的 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代通過一種叫做 " 審判性 " 的對稱性 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度中的這個特殊的載荷圖案事實上是數學中最為漂亮的幾何結構之一
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的例外型李群e8的圖案
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	李群是光滑曲線形的248維度
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	圖案中的每個點都對應到這個非常複雜且漂亮的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的扭曲時空
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	與量子力學一起 , 這個形狀的幾何形狀能夠描述宇宙如何以最小的尺度運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	居住在八度載荷空間中這個形狀的圖案是極其美麗的它總結了數千種這些基本粒子之間可能的相互作用每一種都只是這個複雜形狀的一個表面
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	轉動它時 , 我們可以看到其中有許多錯綜複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	通過某種旋轉我們可以在八度空間沿一個對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何一個統一 , 我們可以看到一些孔 , 在這個圖案中 , 新的粒子會被這種圖案所需要的 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子應該有20個落差 , 其中兩個曾被派蒂姆粒子填補過 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從它們在圖案的位置我們知道這些新粒子應該像是希格斯粒子但擁有色荷且和強力相互作用
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子完成這個圖案 , 給我們完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有著很深的數學根
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個數學美麗的理論可以用最小的尺度來描述粒子相互作用的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	而這個被數學所描述的自然現象並不是全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年 , 伽利略寫了這本書: " 大自然的宏偉書 , 一直對我們的凝視開放 , 用數學的語言寫的 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形 , 和其他的幾何形狀 , 沒有人類無法理解它的單字 ; 若沒有這些 , 就會在黑暗的迷宮中四處遊蕩 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的我曾試過去遵循伽利略的指導只用三角形圓形和其他的幾何形狀來描述粒子物理的數學
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我真的在研究這個東西時 , 數學可以和一個黑暗的迷宮重新聚合 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但讓人放心的是 , 這數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學一起 , 這個數學把我們的宇宙描述為一個在成長的e8珊瑚同時粒子在每個可能的位置相互作用依照美麗的圖案
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	當更多模式運用新型機器 , 例如大型強子對撞機時 , 我們也許可以觀察到大自然是利用e8圖案還是另一種圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程 , 是個很棒的探險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那就太酷了
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果對撞機發現了新粒子但不符合這個圖案那會非常有趣但是對e8理論不利
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那到底有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 還蠻糟的 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然如何運作是個很冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的理論都是很長的投籃動作 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人知道大部分的想法可能不會成真 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣而已:有很多地方是這樣子的 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	如同任何大型投資 , 在不出問題時 , 要放棄一行研究是情感上的困難 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學界 , 如果有什麼不行 , 你就得丟掉它 , 再試試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 唯一能維持理智並達到幸福的方法就是在生命中保持平衡和觀點
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已經竭盡所能地生活著一個平衡的人生 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理、愛和衝浪中平衡我自己的三個載荷方向
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這麼一來 , 就算我所從事的物理工作並沒有什麼成果 , 我仍然知道我已經過了好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	而我試著在美麗的地方居住
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個非常美麗的地方
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	這是我父母最大的一個謎團我如何能在沒有全職工作的情況下生存下來
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要告訴你們這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊島的家庭辦公室的照片
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你們可能已經注意到 , 這些美麗的景色是相似的 , 但在略有不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一個很不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不擔心房租讓我把時間花在喜歡做的事情上 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	過著遊牧生活有時已經很辛苦了 , 但它讓我可以生活在美麗的地方 , 並保持我所樂於生活的平衡 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	讓我可以花大量的時間在超級聰明的珊瑚上 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明人才的公司
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興被邀請來ted演講
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我可能理解其中百分之二的部分 , 但我仍然熱愛它 。 所以我將聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論我很習慣珊瑚理論
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:沒錯 。 讓少數人至少感到興奮的原因是 , 如果你答對了 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是不是說 , 我們應該把宇宙當成一個最小的可能性 , 最小的核心 , 是不是有可能變成e8的可能性 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我是說 , 有最小的比例嗎 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	亨利:嗯 , 我剛剛給你們看的圖案 , 是對應到我們所知的基本粒子物理學 , 它們已經對應到了一個非常美麗的圖形 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這也是我說的我們很確定就知道的事 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這個形狀與e8圖案有著明顯的相似性 , 它所符合的形狀可能就是這張圖的其他部分 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點的圖案實際上代表了這個高維物體在空間中移動的對稱性 , 在我們體驗到的時空中移動和舞蹈 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這也解釋了我們所見的所有這些基本粒子
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克里斯:但是弦理論家 , 正如我所理解的 , 用更小的弦震動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裏面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們應該如何看待電子與e8的關係 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	不對 , 這會是這個e8圖形的對稱之一
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	當這個形狀在時空中移動時 , 會發生扭曲 。 當它在移動時 , 它的扭曲方向就是我們看到的粒子 。 所以...克里斯:e8形狀的大小 , 那和電子的大小有什麼關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	變大了嗎 ? 變小了嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	反之 , 據我們所知 , 電子是點粒子 , 所以它會降到最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 在量子場論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是 , 所有的可能性都在同時展開發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這也是我為什麼拿珊瑚作類比
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8的進入方式是它將如同在時空中每一點附著的形狀一樣 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	如我所說的 , 形狀在經過這個彎曲的表面時 , 會扭曲的方向 , 形狀也就是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	通過量子場理論 , 他們表現出自己的立場並以此方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能再講得更清楚了 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這真的不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它喚起了一種奇蹟的感覺 , 我肯定想了解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但 , 非常謝謝你來 。 非常迷人 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇中的黑猩猩janodall談到tacare和她的其他社群計畫這些計畫能幫助非洲鄉下繁榮的人們與受到威脅的動物並肩同行
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球性議題、污染、靈長類、科學 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍.古德幫助人類和動物生活在一起
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 無論如何 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 節奏 , 晚安 , 晚安 , 但我們也可以ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩的叫聲在晚上他們去睡覺前
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽見它從山谷的一端傳到另一端 , 從一群巢穴傳到另一端 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今晚我想聽我的演講 , 從昨天zeray離開的地方開始 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個了不起、三歲的澳洲學童 , selam 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽說過透過基因側寫人類的歷史、族譜、人類的族譜 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	是一位古生物學家 , 已故的路易思.李奇 , 他讓我走上了研究黑猩猩的道路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	在當時可說是非常了不起 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	這種說法現在普遍存在 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石遺跡 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你能從化石中得知那些人的長相 , 從肌肉的形狀判斷出 , 與他們同住的各種手工藝品 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但它們的行為呢 ? 這是他想知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為也不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張──現在是很普遍的理論 , 如果我們在最接近的居住物種、偉大的猿類及人類身上找到相似的行為模式 , 也許這些行為在七百萬年前就存在了 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們將這些特質從古老遠古時代帶給我們 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看今天的教科書處理人類進化的過程你會經常發現人們依據黑猩猩的行為來推測早期人類的行為
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	他們比其他生物更像我們 , 在ted大會上我們都聽過了 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以對我來說 , 對於黑猩猩是多麼像我們一樣 , 在特定的面向來評論牠們的行為 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每一隻黑猩猩都有他/她自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我會給牠們取名字 。 牠們可以活到60歲以上 , 雖然我們認為大部份的牠們可能不會在野外活到60歲
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲先生 。 雌性在十一或十二歲時就生了第一個孩子 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那之後 , 她每五到六年會生一個小孩 , 在孩童需要護理時 , 晚上和母親一起睡覺 , 背靠著背靠著背 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 這段長時間的童年期對黑猩猩很重要 , 就像是對我們而言 , 與學習息息相關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同形式的動物演化上變得更複雜 , 我們發現學習在個體的生命史中扮演著一個更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察長輩的行為 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們有能力模仿他們看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 用這種方式 , 目前在所有不同黑猩猩族群中 , 已經看到不同的使用工具的行為 , 在非洲各個不同族群中研究 , 這些行為是如何從一個世代傳到下一個世代的 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 這樣我們就可以將這些使用工具的行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口說的語言 。 我們剛剛談過了
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確擁有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 當中有許多是相似的 , 甚至相同的 , 和我們在相同的情境下形成的 。 迎接黑猩猩擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們還親吻 , 手牽手 , 拍彼此的背 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	他們誇大了 , 扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩的社會裡 , 我們發現很多很多的例子都有同情心 , 也有愛心和真正的利他行為 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 對他們的本性有著很黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有著極度殘暴的能力 , 甚至一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常侵略性的行為 , 大部分的情況下 , 都是針對鄰近社會群體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	牠們非常具侵略性 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信黑猩猩 , 比起其它的生物 , 已經讓我們了解 , 畢竟人類和動物世界之間並沒有一條明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 隨著我們做出更多的觀察 , 它每時每刻都在變得更加模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始進行的研究 , 至今仍持續著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些生活在野外的複雜社交生活中的黑猩猩們 , 幫助我們去認識到我們是屬於其中的一部分 , 而不是分開的 , 那些與我們共享地球的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 很遺憾地發現黑猩猩們 , 和世界上其他許多生物一樣 , 正在喪失牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這是一張來自空氣的照片 , 它向你展示了岡貝那森林的高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那時我飛越了整個區域16年前 , 我意識到在公園之外這片森林在1960年 , 幾乎沒有支撐沿著塔根尼科湖東邊的岸邊 , 那是小小的 , 30平方公園國家公園的所在地 , 那是我心目中的一個問題 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 ? 當住在國家公園附近的居民都在掙扎求生存 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	比土地所能容納的還要多的人
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民的數量由蒲隆地和剛果湖逐漸增加 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	而非常貧窮的人們他們負擔不起從其他地方購買食物
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱它為 " 塔托雷 " 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	用一種非常整體的方式來改善住在公園附近村莊的人們的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	從12個村莊開始算小 。 現在是24個村莊 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	時間不夠了 , 但這包含了像是樹木的護理之類的 , 最適合耕種的方法 , 如今已被嚴重損壞 , 幾乎像沙漠一樣的山上種植 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制和預防土壤侵蝕的方法 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	恢復過度使用農地的方式 , 讓兩年內能再生產 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	協助村民們從井裡能取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建造一些學校教室
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 與一小群婦女合作 , 提供她們取得微型貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	如同世界各地的案例 , 大約95%的貸款都歸還了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦權給女性 , 和教育工作 , 提供獎學金給女孩 , 讓他們能完成中學 , 清楚了解這一點 , 在全世界 , 因為女性的教育改善了 , 家庭規模也下降了 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病等資訊
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這個計畫的結果是 , 保育工作的狀況正在發生 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保護區的情況是 , 在這24個村落裡的農夫 , 與其以一群白人來研究猴子──順帶一提 , 很多工作人員現在是坦尚尼亞人──但當我們開始坦尚尼亞造林計劃時 , 卻是一個坦尚尼亞人進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞的團隊與村民對話 , 問他們感興趣的地方 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 ; 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 隨著他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更加了解保育的必要性 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解到山坡的上層被砍伐樹木 , 所以你有這種可怕的土壤流失和爛泥 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展我們所謂的 「 更偉大的岡貝生態系統 」 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這個區域遠在國家公園之外 , 延伸到所有這些惡劣的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落有更好的生活水準時 , 他們實際上同意將百分之十到二十的高地附近的土地放到一旁 , 如此一來 , 當樹木再長回來時 , 黑猩猩們就有可以透過這些樹林傳回來的葉子走廊 , 牠們可以在國家公園外面的基因上和其他殘存的族群互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以塔卡爾是個成功的國家 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們把它複製到非洲的其他區域 , 其它野生的地方 , 都面臨極端的人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們前幾天在ted所討論的問題 , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	貧窮的問題非常嚴重 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你讓大量的人居住在沒有肥沃的土地上 , 特別是當你砍掉樹木 , 讓土壤變得開放 , 導致土壤受到侵蝕 , 隨著絕望的人們砍掉越來越多的樹木 , 這樣他們就可以自己和家人種植食物 , 會發生什麼事 ? 一定要有所貢獻 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	另外一個問題不只在非洲 , 其他的發展中國家還有各地我們對地球做了什麼事 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道的 , 著名的科學家e.o.wilson曾說過假如地球上每一個人都的生活水準歐洲人或美國人 , 我們需要三個新的星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說四個 。 但我們沒有他們 。 我們還有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	到底發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題是 , 我們這裡 , 可以說是走路過地球的最聰明的生物 , 擁有這個非凡的大腦 , 能夠有這麼棒的科技 , 可以這麼好地被這些ted會議所闡述 , 然而 , 我們卻在破壞我們僅有的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	全世界的原住民 , 在他們做了一個重大的決定之前 , 常常坐著問自己: 「 這個決定會如何影響我們未來的七代人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 重大的決定-今天我談的不是非洲 , 而是已開發國家重大的決定 , 包含了數百萬美元 , 數百萬人 , 通常是基於 「 這會如何影響到下一次的股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決定會影響非洲
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲四處旅行 , 談論黑猩猩所面臨的問題 , 以及它們消失的森林 , 我越來越了解到 , 許多非洲的問題在以前的殖民時代是如何被剝削的 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 到歐洲演講 , 到美國演講 , 到亞洲去演講 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你知道我說的那種 , 我說的污染 ,
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們經常呼吸的空氣毒害著我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害著我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水資源或許是其中一個最關鍵的議題這個世紀到處都有水正在被污染由農業、工業和家庭所製成的化學物到處都有這些仍然被噴灑在世界各地似乎是無法從過去體驗獲利的
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 ; 海嘯的效果會愈來愈糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過了土壤的侵蝕 ,
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們不小心燃燒化石燃料 , 同時還有其他溫室氣體 , 被稱為 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界各地 , 人們開始相信有一些事正在發生 , 我們的氣候有問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都被混為一談
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且是那些受到影響較嚴重的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	就是非洲已經受影響了 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的很多地方 , 乾旱的情況更糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨季真的到來時 , 它經常會導致洪水、更加嚴重 , 還有貧窮、飢餓、疾病的惡性循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	而居住在無法支撐的土地上的人數 , 貧窮到無法購買食物 , 因為整片土地都被降解了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會因為最後一棵樹被砍倒而受到沙漠化的感染 , 令人毛骨悚然 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這樣的事不只發生在非洲 , 全世界都一樣
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到了許多失去希望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 失去了原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為在這麼聰明的大腦中 , 可以有某種不連續的聯繫嗎 ? ted技術就是這麼說的 , 人類的心 ? 以非科學的角度來說 , 談論它 , 以愛和同情的角度 。 有沒有什麼不一樣的聯繫 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上 , 他們不是憂鬱或冷漠 , 就是痛苦和憤怒 。 他們說的或多或少是一樣的 , 「 我們會有這種感覺 , 是因為我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 且我們對此無能為力 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每次我看著他們 , 心裡想著我們是如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 從我還是他們的年紀開始 , 我就感受到這種絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這就導致了這個計畫 , 我們稱之為根與芽 , 這個計畫始於坦尚尼亞 , 現在已擴及全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	這很有象徵性 。 根很能建立堅實的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	芽看起來似乎很微小 ; 為了到達太陽 , 它們可以穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	磚牆就如同我們在地球上所面臨的所有問題 , 環境和社會問題 。 這是一個充滿希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地成千上萬的年輕人能夠突破這些世界 , 為所有生物創造出更好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽想傳遞的最重要的訊息是:我們每一個人 , 每天都在做改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每一個人 , 我們都有選擇我們想要做出怎樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	窮人沒有選擇 , 只能靠我們改變 , 讓窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽計畫團體都選擇三個計劃 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們幾歲 , 以及哪個國家 , 無論他們是在城市或鄉村 , 哪種計劃 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼兒園到大學的計畫 , 有越來越多的成人開始他們的根與芽的團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	而每一組都選擇 , 在他們之間三個不同的計畫要讓這個世界更美好 , 了解到所有這些不同的問題都互相連結起來 , 並且在彼此身上不斷進步 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以 , 他們的其中一個計畫 , 將是要協助他們自己的人類社區 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能夠 , 他們就能夠籌措資金 , 幫助世界上其他地區的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助動物 , 不只是野生動物 , 還有家畜 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的其中一個計畫就是要幫助我們所共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	在這一切之中 , 都是一個關於學習如何在和平與和諧中生活的訊息 , 在我們的家庭中、在我們的社區中、在國家之間、在文化之間、在宗教之間 , 和我們之間、在自然世界中 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們不能以我們的速度繼續破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只是挑出一兩個在非洲的項目--根與芽的團體正在進行的項目--在坦尚尼亞 , 烏干達 , 肯亞 , 南非 , 剛果 , 塞拉利昂 , 喀麥隆和其他團體 。 正如我所說的 , 它在世界上97個國家實行 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們種樹 , 種有機蔬菜
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營中工作 , 用小錢賣雞蛋 , 或只用它們來餵飽家庭 , 並感受到一種驕傲和賦權的感覺 , 因為它們不再能助長和依賴別人 , 用它們的蔬菜和雞隻來賣 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理上的幫助 , 給予一些士兵的心理協助 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做像這樣的計畫是把他們自己帶出來 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是有用的社會成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們也在監獄裡有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有更多根與芽的時機 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽計畫的重要組成部分 , 讓年齡較長的孩子和年紀較小的孩子說話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	而未成年的懷孕和類似的事情 , 也就是年輕人會更傾聽年輕人的心聲 , 而不是成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 那是我在世界各地會被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你見過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你見到你的黑猩猩們在世紀末將數量減少從一百萬、一百五十萬 , 甚至其他許多動物身上也一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 曾經是森林的沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? " 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted一樣沒有希望的會議 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是這令人驚嘆的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想看科技
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	最後 , 我非常興奮能夠來到人們談論堆肥式的公廁 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	它是我的一個嗜好 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只是把所有的水往馬桶裡沖 , 真是糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	再來談再生能源極為重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否為我們的孩子關心地球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	我們有多少人有小孩、孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們在乎他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	假如我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為這世界上精英份子 , 我們可以做點什麼 。 我們可以選擇如何過日子 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼、穿什麼
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇以問題做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	會如何影響我的孩子在他或她成長過程中
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 或不管是什麼
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以人腦 , 與人心結合 , 我們加入世界各地的人腦 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這就是ted對此的幫助 , google也幫助我們 , esri也幫助我們繪製岡貝國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的技術
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 而它也開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	今天下午你們已經聽過了 , 現在已經開始發生了
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這樣的改變 , 這樣的改變 。 如果我們關心未來 , 我們一定要看到這些改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	下一個原因是希望大自然有驚人的恢復力 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以將一個絕對毀滅的地區 , 利用時間 , 也許還能協助它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	而一個例子是塔卡爾計畫
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我說過 , 看似死去的樹木殘骸 , 如果你不再為了生火而駭入 , 那你也不需要因為你擁有很多的木材 , 然後在五年之內 , 你就可以有一棵三十英呎高的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	幾乎絕種的動物 , 都可以得到第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	這是很鼓舞人心的 。 這也帶到了我最後一個希望類別 。 過去兩天我們已經聽說了這麼多關於這個不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這種對人類精神的堅韌決心 , 以致那些你認為會被貧窮 , 或疾病所擊垮的人們 , 或為此類的事情 , 有時還能將他們自己從中吸取 , 有時只要一個幫忙 , 把他們的部份帶到社會上 , 讓他們能夠參與改變這個世界 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想那些真正鼓舞人心的非洲人物 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出很長的清單 , 但很明顯的 , 納爾遜•曼德拉從17年的辛苦勞工、23年的監禁 , 帶著這種驚人的寬恕能力 , 讓他能夠帶領他的國家走出沒有流血的種族隔離政權 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	kensarowiwa , 奈及利亞的大型石油公司 , 雖然世界各地的人竭盡所能 , 卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣子的人們是如此鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人就是我們年輕非洲人所需要的典範 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 我今天也已經聽過了一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我真的很感激有這個機會再次和ted的每個人分享這個訊息
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們中的一些人能聚在一起討論這些事 , 特別是根與芽的計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後我要跟那位經營整個會議中心的年輕女子談個最後 , 我今天遇到了她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她上來時非常興奮 , 靠的是她的認證 。 她是根與芽的 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在daressalaam的領導階層
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這可以幫助她做到她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 非常振奮人心 , 讓我看到一個例子 , 說明年輕人在被賦予能力時 , 能夠有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更好 , 真正是我們對明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家狄安娜•柯恩分享了一些堅韌的真理 , 關於海洋和生活中的塑膠污染 , 以及一些關於如何把我們自己從塑膠漩渦中解放出來的思想 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球性議題、綠色、使命藍藍、海洋、塑膠製品 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	diannacohen:關於塑膠污染的堅硬真相
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 同時也是塑膠污染聯盟的發起人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在使用塑膠袋 , 我剪開和縫合 , 做為我藝術作品的主要材料 , 已有二十年了 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二維和三維的雕塑和裝置藝術
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	前八年我的工作開始產生裂縫 , 分解成更小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太棒了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	跟我們一樣 , 是短暫的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	等我讓自己對塑膠有進一步的了解其實這是件壞事
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	這是塑膠分解成小塊的壞東西因為它總是塑膠的
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 很多生物都在海洋環境裡 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	在過去幾年 , 我得知了太平洋垃圾環流和垃圾漩渦 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	而我最初的反應我想 , 很多人的第一反應就是學習它 , 「 天哪 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得走出去把這個東西清理乾淨 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以我真的提出了一個提案 , 去搭配一艘貨物船 , 和兩艘退休的漁船、一座起重機、一台割草機 , 以及一台冷模機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我打算去到垃圾場 , 提高人們對這個議題的認知 , 開始拿起塑膠 , 把它切成一小塊碎片 , 再冷卻 , 做成磚塊 , 在未開發的社區中可能被用來當作建材 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始跟那些真的去過垃圾漩渦星球的人談話他們正在研究海洋裡的塑膠問題接著我了解到 , 把塑膠清理乾淨是和全世界每天產生的量比起來是一小滴事實上 , 我需要退一步仔細觀察這大局
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	而更大的情況是:我們需要找到一種方式來關掉水龍頭 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要去除那些用過即丟的塑膠製品 , 這些塑膠每天都進入海洋環境 , 以全球性的規模進入 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著這一點 , 我也了解到 , 我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心到塑膠你還會想象在太平洋中間的塑膠 。 我發現現在有11個塑膠垃圾漩渦遍佈全球五大洋 。
