so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	他確實是將雙向音頻和影片串在任何兩個智慧型裝置之間 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	所以你可以透過瀏覽器來登入 , 有點像skype一樣的輪子 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	我們之前談到遠端臨場感 , 這裡有個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲大的女孩 , 例如 , 她有一支iphone , 她媽媽會買給她一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿著她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 寄一封電子郵件給祖母 , 她住在國家的另一邊 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩捉迷藏 , 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她一年可能只能去看她孫女一次或兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	所以這些是romo今天能做的幾個很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	最後我想談談我們未來在努力的方向 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這實際上是我們的一個工程師 , dom , 在一個週末裡建造的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google一個稱為blockly的開放框架上的 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這可以讓你拖拉這些區塊的編碼以及為這個機器人創造任何你想要的行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何代碼去為romo創造一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你實際上可以在瀏覽器中去模擬這種行為 , 就是你看到romo在左邊做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以下載它到你的機器人 , 在現實生活中執行它 , 在現實生活中執行該程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有什麼值得驕傲的你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些無線網路的機器人 , 其實可以互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以如此重視如何建造一個大家都能訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人中 , 最能引人注目的用法是個人化的 。
they change from person to person .	它們會從人變成人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你要在你的家中有個機器人 , 那個機器人應該是你自己想像出來的一種呈現出來 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以 , 我希望我能告訴你們個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我也不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但是我們確實知道的是 , 它不是10年或100億美元 , 也不是一個大型的類人機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來就發生在今天 , 它取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 像是romo , 以及像你們這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以我們等不及要你們所有的機器人 , 我們等不及要看看你們建造了什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和行動主義者伊莎貝•阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有這場演講的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女人、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德講述關於激情的故事
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你們 。 站在這裡真可怕有這麼一個聰明的人
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我在這裡告訴你們幾個充滿熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有個猶太人說我愛
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	比真理更真誠的是什麼 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是一個說故事的人 。 我想要傳達一個比事實更真實的東西 , 關於我們共同的人性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都對我感興趣 , 有些則縈繞在我心頭 , 直到最後我寫下它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們周遭的神祕 , 所以我寫下巧合、預兆、情緒、夢想、自然的力量、魔力 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但是我一直活在匿名中 , 直到2006年2月 , 那時我負責在義大利的冬季奧運會 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成了名人 。 現在大家在macy的領域裡認得我 , 我的孫子們都覺得我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	容我在此說說我的四分鐘名氣
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	一名籌辦奧運開幕式的籌辦人打電話給我說我被選為護旗手之一
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答 , 這肯定是個錯誤認同的案例 , 因為我離運動員越遠越好 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	其實 , 我甚至不確定我可以到體育館 , 不用助行器 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是在笑
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這會是第一次只有女性會帶著奧林匹克旗幟
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五名女性 , 代表五大洲 , 和三名奧運金牌得主 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說一件制服 , 並尋求我的衡量標準 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我有一個願景 , 一個蓬鬆的大動脈 , 看起來就像米其林男子一樣 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了2月中旬 , 我發現自己身在杜林 , 在那裡 , 充滿熱情的群眾在街上獲得80個奧運團體歡呼 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	這些運動員犧牲了在遊戲中競爭的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都應得勝利 , 但有運氣的元素
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一陣冰雪、一英吋的冰、一股風力 , 可以決定比賽的結果或比賽的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的是訓練或是運氣是心 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才能得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	一切都和熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	杜林街上滿是紅色海報 , 宣布奧運的標語 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情就在這裡 。 難道不是一直都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們及決定我們的命運的原因 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我書中角色所需要的:充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要改造馬桶、異議者、冒險家、外來者和反抗者 , 他們會問問題、彎曲規則 , 並承擔風險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有常識的好人不會做出有趣的人物 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會做好前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育館的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了其他護旗手:三位運動員 , 演員蘇珊莎蘭登和蘇菲雅羅蘭 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	還有兩位心中充滿熱情的女性:旺加里•馬塔伊 , 肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種植了三千萬棵樹 。 透過這麼做 , 她已經改變了土壤、天氣、非洲的某些地方 , 當然也改變了很多村莊的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	還有柬埔寨行動派女子蘇曼麗•瑪姆 , 她熱情地對抗兒童賣淫 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	她14歲時 , 祖父將她賣到妓院
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴 , 她們相信和年紀很小的處女做愛可以治好愛滋病 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	而妓院裡的孩童們 , 每天被迫接收五、十五個客戶如果他們反抗 , 就會被電擊折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色的房間裡我收到制服
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這可不是我平常穿的那種衣服 , 卻離我預期的米其林男裝的那件 。 其實不錯 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但大部分的旗幟都是 , 除了蘇菲雅羅蘭 , 通用的美麗和熱情的象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感、很渺小 , 且很高 , 有著很深的坦率 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	你怎麼能有一根深色的棕櫚樹 , 卻沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當電視訪談中問到: 「 她怎麼能看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回說: 「 姿勢 。 我的背總是直直的 。 我沒有發出老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 你們有一些免費的建議來自地球上最美麗的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	不乏鬥志、咳嗽、不自言自語、不放屁 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有說得很清楚 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	大概在午夜的時候 , 我們被傳送到體育館的翼手上 , 擴音機也宣佈奧林匹克旗 , 音樂也從這裡開始 , 同樣的音樂就是在這裡開始的 , 愛達大遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她的身高比我高 , 頭髮數不清 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走著 , 就像非洲草原上的長頸鹿將旗子舉在肩上 。 我在後面小跑步 , 用手臂撐著旗子 , 這樣我的頭就在那該死的旗子下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	所有的攝影機當然是 , 在蘇菲雅
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	那對我來說是幸運的 , 因為大部分刊登的照片都是我出現的 , 雖然常常是發生在蘇菲雅的雙腳之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個多數人都很喜歡去的地方
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的4分鐘就是那些在奧運體育館裡
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我丈夫被冒犯了雖然我跟他解釋說我們私下作的事通常要花不到四分鐘所以他不應該獨自承受
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我擁有那四個偉大的分鐘數的所有按鈕 , 因為我不想忘記當年紀漸漸摧毀我的腦細胞的時候 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想要永遠帶著奧運的關鍵字 「 熱情 」 。
so here's a tale of passion .	以下是關於熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	時間是1998年 , 地點是一座囚營 , 供應了剛果的圖西族難民 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順帶一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所的人都是婦女和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱這個地方為剛果的死亡集中營 , 因為沒有被殺的人 , 會死於疾病或餓死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女性蘿絲•瑪班多和她的孩子
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了 , 有個寡婦
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵迫使她眼睜睜睜看著她的丈夫被虐待並被殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她成功讓她的七個孩子活了下來 , 幾個月後 , 她生了早產兒 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子自己割斷臍帶然後用頭髮把它綁起來
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她以營地指揮官的名字命名 , 以獲得他們的喜好 , 並用黑色茶餵食給他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持他們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵闖進她的牢房要強暴她大女兒時 , 她會抓住她並拒絕放手 , 即使他們拿著槍抵著她的頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家人存活了16個月然後 , 靠著絕佳的運氣和一名美國年輕人的熱心 , 薩夏•查諾夫將她送進美國救援機 , 蘿絲•馬班多和她的九個孩子最後都住在亞利桑那州鳳凰城他們現在的生活和成長茁壯
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	瑪班多在斯瓦希里語中的意思是偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角都是堅強且富熱情的女子 , 就像蘿絲•瑪班多 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不會編出來 , 不需要這些 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處看到它們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在為女性和女性工作 。
i know them well .	我很了解他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在遠古的時期 , 在世界末日 , 在一個父系的天主教及保守家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪五歲時我是個憤怒的女權主義者雖然現在還沒有到智利這個名詞所以沒有人知道我到底是怎麼搞的
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	很快地 , 我就會發現 , 有很高的代價可以支付我的自由 , 以及對父權提出質疑 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付出 , 因為每次我接到的一擊 , 我都能遞出二分錢 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我的女兒寶拉在她二十多歲時 , 她對我說女權主義已經約會了 , 我該繼續下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們曾打過一場難忘的仗 。 女性主義是約會的嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於我女兒和在場的所有人來說 , 是的 , 但對其他地方的姊妹們來說 , 仍然被迫結婚、賣淫、強迫勞動──他們有自己不想要的孩子 , 或無法進食的孩子 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法掌控自己的身體或人生 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育和自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、毆打 , 有時被懲罰殺 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	現今大部分的西方年輕女性 , 被稱為女權主義者是一種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權從來就不吸引人 , 但 , 讓我向各位保證 , 它從來就不會阻止我調情 , 我很少有缺乏男性的痛苦 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女權主義沒有死 , 絕對沒有 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞 , 它就改變了它 , 為了女神的緣故 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	把它叫作aphrodite , 或維納斯 , 或布波 , 或任何你想要的 , 名字都無所謂 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	所以這又是一個關於熱情的故事 , 這是另一個令人難過的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉某個村落的一間小型女性診所
the year is 2005 .	那一年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是個年輕的美國牙醫醫 , 在她三週的假期間 , 已經進入診所當義工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她早就準備好了乾淨的牙齒了 , 但當她到那裡的時候 , 她發現那裡沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一個充滿蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一行婦女等了幾個小時才被醫治 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一個病人痛苦難當因為她好幾個腐爛的臼齒
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮意識到唯一的解決方案就是拔掉不好的牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有授權她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她的風險很大 , 她嚇壞了 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她連適當的樂器都沒有 , 但幸好她已經帶了一些麻醉藥 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有顆勇敢和熱情的心
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她怒罵了一個祈禱者 , 然後繼續營運 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病人鬆了一口氣 , 親了她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天衛生學家多拔了牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 當她再次來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人在跟她丈夫等候 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	這女人的臉看起來像是個西瓜 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	腫到看不見眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫氣極了 , 威脅要殺了美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做的事感到恐懼 , 但接著 , 翻譯解釋病人的狀況與手術無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她丈夫打她因為她沒有家為他準備晚餐
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬女性過著這樣的生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最貧窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然女性分擔世界上三分之二的勞力 , 但她們擁有的資產卻不到世界財產的1% 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	她們的薪水低於男性 , 如果她們有薪水 , 她們仍然是弱勢 , 因為她們沒有經濟獨立 , 且她們不斷受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實是 , 給予女性教育、工作、控制自己收入的能力、繼承並擁有財產 , 讓社會受惠 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予能力 , 她的孩子和家人會變得更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落也會繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家也一樣 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	旺加里•馬塔伊去肯亞的一個村落
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女們談話 , 解釋說 , 土地已經貧瘠了 , 因為他們砍了樹並賣了樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓女人們種植新的樹 , 澆水 , 滴一滴 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在僅僅5或6年的時間裡他們就有了森林 , 土壤豐富了 , 村子因而得救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最落後的社會 , 總是那些讓女性放下身段的人 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而 , 這個顯而易見的事實卻被政府及慈善機構忽視 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	以婦女計劃的費用 , 每捐20美元就有20美元給男性 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔了人類的51% 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	給予他們力量將比科技、設計和娛樂更能改變一切
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性同心協力連結、有知覺、受過教育的女性 , 能為這個盛行的星球帶來和平與繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	今天的任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡者是平民 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 他們是附帶傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人跑世界 , 看看我們這一團糟 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要怎樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是大多數人都在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序合理嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們要一個保存生命的世界以及生活品質能夠豐富所有人 , 而不僅僅是為了特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月我看到費南多•波特羅在加州大學伯克利圖書館的畫展
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國沒有一間博物館或畫廊除了紐約畫廊背負著巴特羅的作品而且膽敢展示這幅畫因為這個主題是阿布格萊布監獄
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	他們是巨大的畫作 , 畫的是虐待和權力的畫作 , 用的是大量的博特羅風格 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法把那些影像從我的腦海裡或心中顯現出來 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	最讓我害怕的是充滿力量的權力 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個族群 , 雄性領袖定義了現實 , 逼迫其他成員接受現實並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則常常在改變 , 但總是有好處 , 在這種情況下 , 在經濟上行不通的 「 下滲效應 」 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	從最上面的梯子到最下面的梯子 , 爬下來了 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	婦女和兒童 , 尤其是窮人 , 都位於海底 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最貧窮的男人也有人可以虐待女人或小孩
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我受夠了少數人用的力量 , 透過性別、收入、種族和階級 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為現在時機已經成熟 , 可以在我們的文明中做出根本性的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 若要真正改變 , 我們就需要在世界管理階層的女性能量 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要讓一定數量的女性掌握權力我們需要培養男性心中的女性能量
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我說的當然是有年輕心智的男性 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老傢伙是沒有希望的 ; 我們得等他們死掉 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想擁有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿以及傳奇的乳房 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 就一個選擇來說 , 我寧願有顆勇士的心 , 像旺加里•馬塔伊、索瑪利、珍妮和蘿絲•瑪班多 。
i want to make this world good .	我想要讓這個世界變好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是讓它良好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不呢 ? 這是有可能的 。 看看這間房間裡所有的知識、能量、才華和科技
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	放下我們的歌迷吧 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地投入工作 , 創造一個近乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦這麼大的城市中 , 有三千萬份餐是用在的 。 但是 , 所有的食物是從哪裡來的呢 ? 建築師carolynsteel正討論要餵飽一個城市的每日奇蹟 , 並顯示古老的食物路線如何塑造了現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	carolynsteel:食物如何塑造我們的城市
how do you feed a city ?	如何餵飽一個城市
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代最偉大的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但很少被問到
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們理所當然地認為 , 如果我們去商店或餐廳 , 或在一小時內到戲院大廳 , 那裡將會有食物等待著我們 , 神奇地從某處來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但 , 當你想到倫敦這麼大的城市 , 每天都有足夠的食物被製造、運送、買、賣、煮、吃、處理 , 類似的現象 , 日復一日發生在地球上的每個城市中 , 這一切都很了不起 , 城市能被餵飽 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們居住的地方 , 彷彿它們是世界上最自然的東西 , 忘記了我們是動物、我們需要進食的地方 , 我們其實和我們古老的祖先一樣依賴自然世界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	當更多人搬進城市 , 更多的自然世界被改造成非凡的景色 , 就像我身後的這個 , 是巴西馬托格羅索的大豆田 , 目的是要餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些景色很特別 , 但少有人見識過 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	愈來愈多的風景不只是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	當更多人搬進城市時 , 更多人會吃肉 , 每年全球的穀物作物有三分之一都被餵食給動物 , 而非我們人類的動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	因為要攝取三倍的穀物實際上要攝取十倍的穀物才能餵飽人 , 如果它先通過動物的話 , 那就不是很有效的供養方式 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個不斷增長的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 估計我們生活在城市中的人數會是現在的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	同時估計將會有兩倍的肉類和乳製品
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉類和都市主義在手上興起 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會是個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	要餵飽六十億個肉食性動物到2050年
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 而事實上 , 如果我們以現狀繼續走下去 , 這個問題我們就不太可能解決 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有一千九百萬公頃的熱帶雨林消失 , 無法創造出新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然我們同時也失去相當於現有的可耕地在鹽化及侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也非常渴望石化燃料
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	在西方每製造一卡路里的食物要耗去大約10卡路里
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管有糧食供給我們帶來極大的成本我們卻不重視
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	半數在美國生產的食物 , 目前已經被丟棄 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	要終結這一切 , 在這漫長過程的最後 , 我們甚至還沒有妥善地供應食物給地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們當中有十億人過度肥胖 , 同時又又又有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這一切都不太合理
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為現在全球百分之八十的食物交易只由五大跨國公司所掌控這真是個死板
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們遷入城市 , 世界也開始擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們展望未來 , 這是個不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答稍微容易一點的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說是這個過程的開端 , 就在古老的近東地區 , 也就是所謂的新月沃土 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它的形狀
and it was also fertile .	同時也很肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 在這裡 , 有兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和城市化 , 大約在同一地點、同一時間出現 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市是分不開的 。 他們互相需要
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老祖先首次發現的穀物 , 它能產生足夠大量且穩定的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久居住 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看那些居住地的樣子 , 我們會發現它們是緊實的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被農田圍繞並支配像這一個在烏爾的大型寺廟這樣的大型寺廟 , 實際上是心靈分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是神殿安排了收割 , 聚集在穀物裡 , 將之獻給神 , 然後再提供給神沒吃下的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以如果你願意 , 這些城市的精神及實體生活是由他們賴以爲生的穀物和收成所支配 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老的城市也是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	著名的是 , 早在西元一世紀時羅馬就有大約一百萬的居民
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	那麼像這樣的城市是怎麼養得出來的呢 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案就在我所謂的 " 古代食物里程 "
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬接觸大海 , 因而得以從很遠很遠的地方運送食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在遠古時期 , 唯一可能做到這件事的方式 , 因為運送食物是很困難的 , 這很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物顯然很快就掉下來了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效地攻擊比如車庫、埃及之類的地方 , 只為了拍到它的爪子儲備 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說這個帝國的擴張真的是一場漫長 , 真的是一場軍事化的購物 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到這個:羅馬還曾經從倫敦運輸牡蠣 , 到一個階段我想那是很不尋常的
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬藉著它的胃口塑造了牠的腦部
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事情也發生在工業化前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看十七世紀的倫敦地圖我們可以看到它的穀物是從泰晤士河運入在這張地圖的下方
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場都是在市中心的南方
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	而道路從它們變成廉價的 , 也是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以看出三百年前那裡發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	魚也是一樣 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是由河流進來的 。 同樣的事情 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , billingsgate最有名的是倫敦的魚市場一直到1980年代中期都還在使用
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這真的很特別 , 真的 , 當你想到
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	所有其他人都帶著手機遊蕩 , 看起來像磚頭 , 還有有點臭的魚在港口沿著 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是城市食物的另一件事:一旦它的根源被建立起來 , 幾乎不會再移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類的故事不同 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	所以倫敦的大部分肉品是從西北方來的從蘇格蘭及威爾斯
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它來了 , 抵達西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常著名的肉市場 , 它就位在那裡 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽類從東安格利亞進來 , 一直到東北方 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得這有點像氣象女子在做這件事 。 不管怎樣 , 鳥兒都帶著腳進來 , 用小的帆布保護鞋進來 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當他們碰到便宜東部的那邊時 , 他們就被賣掉了 , 這就是所謂的 " 家禽 " 的原因 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看一下工業時代前所建的任何城市地圖 , 你可以追蹤食物的來源 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你實際上可以看到它是如何被食物塑造的 , 通過閱讀街道的名稱 , 這給你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在以前是你在星期五去買魚的地方
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但同時你也必須想像 , 它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一一處買賣食物的地方
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的圖片 , 你可以看到 , 住在這樣一個城市 , 很難看清你的食物從哪裡來 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在吃禮拜日午餐 , 可能在你的窗戶外面流血的機率大約是三天前 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	所以這顯然是一個有機的城市 , 是一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	然後十年後一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西部的照片
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	你們可以看到 , 最早的火車乘客當中有一些是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 ,
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被視線和心靈屠殺 , 在鄉下的某處 ,
and they're coming into the city by rail .	並且藉由鐵路來到城市
and this changes everything .	而這會改變一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 這使得我們第一次能夠在任何地方種植城市 , 真正的大小和形狀 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去 , 城市受限於地理條件 ; 過去 , 他們得要用非常困難的實體手段來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們從地理限制中大解放 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	正如你從這些倫敦的地圖上可以看到在火車通行的90年後倫敦從一個容易餵飽的小點一個動物靠著腳步行進食的小點點點等等 , 再到一個大型噴泉那會非常非常非常難餵飽和任何人一起吃足 , 不論是動物或是人
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是開端 。 火車之後又來了汽車 , 這真的是過程的結尾 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	這是城市最終的解放完全從大自然的任何外觀的關係中解放 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	而這正是那種沒有嗅覺的城市 , 沒有混亂 , 肯定也沒有人理會的城市 , 因為沒有人會夢想要走在這樣的地景中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們為了取得食物而做的是他們上了車 , 開到郊區的某個箱子上 , 帶回一星期的購物中心 , 然後想一下 , 到底在地球上用它來做什麼 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	此時此刻 , 我們與食物和城市的關係已完全改變 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有曾經是中心的食物 , 是邊緣的城市的社交核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	以前是社交活動 , 買賣食物
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前只煮菜現在只需要加點水或點點蛋如果你在做蛋糕或什麼的
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們聞不到食物 , 看牠是不是可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只需要讀包裝背後的一個標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而且我們不重視食物 。 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	我們不珍視它 , 而是丟掉它 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統最諷刺的一點是 , 它們已經把他們原本的理想變得更加困難 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由讓城市可以在任何地方及任何地方建立 , 它們其實已經把我們和我們最重要的關係保持距離了 , 那就是我們和大自然的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	此外 , 它們也讓我們依賴只有它們能提供的系統 , 如我們所見 , 它們是無法永續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那麼 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是個新問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前湯瑪斯•摩爾就在問他自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》的前身
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	那是一系列半自主的城邦 , 如果聽起來很熟悉 , 一天走來走去 , 每個人都在農場種植蔬菜 , 在他們的後院種植蔬菜 , 一起吃公用餐等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你們可以主張食物是烏托邦的基本原則 , 即使更多的食物從來沒有這樣看過 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這是另一個非常著名的烏托邦 , ebenezerhoward , 《花園城市》 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一連串的半自立城邦 , 小型的都會區 , 周圍有可耕地的土地 , 彼此連結 , 用鐵路連接彼此 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次地 , 食物可以被說是他願景的訂定原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	甚至建造了 , 但和默斯克韋茲的願景無關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這些烏托邦理念的問題就是他們是烏托邦人
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是一個湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意使用的詞
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為希臘文裏有雙重含義
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可能意味著一個好的地方 , 或沒有好的地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為它是理想的 。 這是個幻想的事情 。 我們無法擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 做為一種概念 , 來思考人類居住的深層問題 , 讓它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了另一個選擇 , 希托邦來自古希臘 , 「 希托 」 代表 「 食物 」 , 「 地點 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在希托邦
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個被食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們意識到這點 , 我們就可以把食物當作十分強大的工具一個概念性的工具 , 設計工具 , 來改變這個世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , 希托邦會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	嗯 , 我覺得它看起來有點像這樣
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 。 這只是狗的臉上的表情 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	但無論如何 , 這裡是生活的中心食物 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌 , 被享用 , 人們花時間在這上面 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這是食物應該在我們的社會所在 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不可能有這樣的場景除非你有這樣的人
by the way , these can be men as well .	順帶一提 , 這些也可以是男人
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	就是大家會想到食物 , 會先計畫、會盯著一堆生菜 , 其實還能認得它們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 。 我們是網絡的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有了這一類的人 , 我們就不可能擁有這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	我故意選這張是因為這是男人在買菜
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但是網絡 , 在本地種植糧食的市場
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	成為社交生活的一部分
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為沒有了這些 , 你就不能擁有這樣的地方 , 本地種植的食物 , 同時也是風景的一部分 , 不僅僅是一些看不見的地獄區段的零和商品 。
cows with a view .	牛帶著景觀
steaming piles of humus .	串流成一堆的嗡嗡聲 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把整件事湊在一起
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪的一個社區專案 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一種溫室 , 孩子們會被告知有關食物的一切 , 並自己種植食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一種叫凱文的植物 , 或者說可能是屬於一個叫凱文的小孩 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這類計畫正試圖將我們與大自然重新連結 , 是非常重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 希托邦對我而言 , 真的是一種看法 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上就是承認希托邦已經存在於小口袋中 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅是要加入他們 , 把食物當作一種看待的方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們將不再將城市視為大型、大都市、沒有生產力的區塊 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像 , 做為生產性有機體架構的一部分 , 它們無可避免地是一部分 , 具有共生的連接 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然 , 這也不是很好的圖像 , 因為我們再也不用像這樣在生産食物了 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更加考慮永續栽培 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張影像可以為我下結論 , 我們要做的那種思考 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	重新思考食物如何改變我們的生活
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我知道最好的圖像來自650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	安布羅吉歐•羅倫澤提的《好政府的寓言》
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	關於城市和鄉間的關係 ,
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這件事情的訊息非常清楚
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧國家 , 國家會照顧城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	現在我想問大家 , 如果他今天畫這張圖 , 安布洛吉歐•洛倫澤蒂會怎麼樣 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	優秀政府的寓言會是什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個急迫的問題
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃什麼
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要意識到這世界也是我們所吃下的
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採用這個想法 , 我們可以用食物來當作很強大的工具 , 來更好地形塑這個世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	在《慈悲發射》的憲章幾週後 , karenarmstrong在二十一世紀探討了宗教的角色:它的教條將我們分割開來嗎 ? 或者它將使我們團結一致嗎 ? 她檢視這些催化劑讓世界的信仰重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝、ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal2009年的暴力 ,
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們復興黃金法則
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我一直感到沮喪 , 因為 , 身為宗教歷史學家 , 我已經敏銳地意識到 , 憐憫是世界主要信仰的中心思想 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一種都自行演化為 " 黃金法則 "
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時候會出現一個正面的版本 " 一如既往般地對待其他人 。 "
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面版的 「 不要對其他人做出你不想對他們做的事情 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心 , 發現什麼讓你痛苦 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 去對別人造成痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	而且人們強調了慈悲的重要 , 不只因為它很好聽 , 更是因為它有效 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了黃金法則如同孔子所說的: 「 一整天、每一天、每一天 」 , 不只是一個關於做好事的問題 , 然後又回到貪婪和自大的一生 , 而是要做一整天 , 每天都在做 , 你把自己從世界的中心、另一個世界、然後超越自我 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它會讓你進入被稱為神的存在 , 涅盤 , 拉馬 , 泰羅 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所認知的範圍
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你也知道 , 很多時候你從來不知道這對宗教生活來說是很重要的
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些美妙的例外 , 通常當宗教人士聚在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起時 , 他們在爭論的是廢除教條或是指出仇恨 , 或是違背同性戀之類的 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們並不真的想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我對一群宗教人士發聲時 , 我會看到 , 一邊是雙邊的表情一邊是雙邊的 , 因為人們常常希望對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然是違反了運動的對象 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	我為什麽要感謝ted呢 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們輕柔地帶領我從我的書籍研究中 , 帶我進入二十一世紀 , 讓我能夠和更廣大的觀眾交談 , 比我想像中更廣闊的觀眾 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我覺得這件事很急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不想辦法在全球實施黃金法則 , 這樣我們就對待所有人 , 不管在哪裡 , 不管他們是誰 , 如同我們自己一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 來交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代的一個偉大的任務 , 就是建立一個全球化的社會 , 如同我所說的 , 人們可以和平地生活在一起 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該要做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 反而被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然也不是只有虔誠的人才信奉黃金法則
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這種富有想像力的同理心行為 , 把自己置於另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 在我看來
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續帶領或強調我們信仰的教條和寬容或者我們可以回到拉比聖母的老年人拉比希爾上來他問一位異教徒他站在一條腿上時要總結整個猶太人的教義並說: 「 這樣做對你來說是可恨的 , 不要對你的鄰居做不好 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	這就是教義 , 其他都只是評論而已 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	而拉比和早期教會的父親們 , 他們說任何對聖經中的仇恨和輕視的詮釋都是違法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們需要復興這樣的精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不僅僅因為一股愛情的精神喚醒了我們
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這件事成真 , 能用ted所引發的現代通訊技術實現它 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對我們所有夥伴的回應感到極大的鼓舞 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一組人打算用憲章來治癒分歧 , 最近在新加坡社會中出現 , 議會的一些成員也希望將憲章用在政治上 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將來會有一場藝術展覽 , 主導藝術家的人會把人 , 年輕人 , 給他們看 , 同情也存在於所有藝術的根源上 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 各個穆斯林社群舉辦活動和討論會 , 討論以伊斯蘭和所有信仰為核心的慈悲心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能就此停止 。 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教的教誨 , 在這裡我們走錯了路 , 專注於相信深奧的教義 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教的教誨一定會導致行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算在這個快要死去的日子裡工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我還想繼續跟我們的夥伴一起做兩件事--去教育和刺激同情心的思想 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育是因為我們已經失去了同情心 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常常覺得這意味著對某人感到抱歉 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但你當然不懂憐憫之心如果你只是想一想
you also have to do it .	你也要做
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望媒體能參與其中 , 因為媒體很重要 , 能協助破除我們對其他人的一些刻板印象 , 那些把我們和其他人分開的刻板印象 。
the same applies to educators .	教育人士也同樣適用
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能夠感受到一種富有同情心的生活方式的活力與挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到 , 它需要敏銳的智慧 , 而非單純的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想要呼籲學者去探索他們自己以及他人的傳統中關於同情的主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	更重要的是 , 要激起一股對無情說話的敏感度 , 這麼一來 , 由於人們有這個憲章 , 不論他們的信仰為何 , 或缺乏他們的信仰 , 他們感到充滿力量去挑戰那些不合情理的言論 , 那些不合理的言論 , 來自他們的宗教領袖、他們的政治領袖、來自產業界的長官 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力 。
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從沒想過將憲章放上網
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我還困在舊世界裡 , 認為一群小傢伙坐在一間房間裡 , 發出另一種神秘的聲明 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	而ted為我介紹了一種全新的思維和呈現想法的方式 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這是ted美妙的地方 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有的專業知識 , 如果我們能一同加入這一切 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 這些問題有時看起來很明顯 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	最後我想引用一位英國作家 , 牛津作家 , 我不常引用c.s.路易斯的話 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫過一件事 , 一直在我心中揮之不去 , 自我還是個學生時 ,
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的《四種愛》書中
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他區別了愛情 , 當兩個人凝視彼此 , 咒罵對方的眼睛時 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	然後他把這段感情與友情比較 , 當兩個人站在一旁時 , 肩並肩 , 雙眼固定在共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我強烈地感受到這一點 , 在我們深思熟慮後 , 當各種不同的說服者聚集在一起 , 一起為共同的目標努力 , 差異就融化了 。
and we learn amity .	並學習艾美 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學著一起生活 , 互相認識

macarthur grant , art , arts , book , cities , communication , culture , design , entertainment , humor , storytelling	麥克阿瑟•格蘭特 , 藝術 , 藝術 , 書 , 城市 , 通訊 , 文化 , 設計 , 娛樂 , 幽默 , 說故事 。

sometimes i make a lot of drawings and i still don't understand what it is i'm drawing .	有時我畫了很多圖 , 我仍然不明白我到底畫了些什麼 。

so , whenever given an opportunity , i try to do something in it or with it or for it .	所以 , 只要有機會 , 我就會試著在當中做點什麼 , 或是用它來做點什麼 。

part of the reason for that is the fact that they grew up organically .	部分原因是因為他們是有機地長大 。
that amazing juxtaposition of old and new , the bits of light that come down between the buildings that sort of create a map that's traveling above your head of usually blue especially in the summer compared to the map that you would normally expect to see of conventional streets .	那神奇的對照──舊和新 , 那些從建築中下來的小光點──這有點像是在你頭頂上方移動的地圖──通常是藍色的 , 尤其是在夏天 , 相較於你平常會在街上看到的地圖 。

a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書並不只是用整齊的方式來收集和儲存資訊 , 而是用一系列的層次 。

the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬的大部分建築用牆面的黏液遮住了傷疤 ; 數世紀來 , 改變的疤痕是被改造而不是被拆除的 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊的一個摺疊頁 , 讓你們看看它的背後 , 我是指傷口組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 做更小的窗戶就變得很重要因為壞人都來了或別的 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應力全都被埋在黏液之下

you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把你頭上的頁面包起來 , 就在那段時間裡那個廣場上 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我沒有做過什麼比摺疊頁更複雜的東西 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但後來我想 , 也許我可以簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	我們來看看萬神殿和前面的羅通達廣場
here's a book completely wide open .	這裡有一本完全開放的書
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不把書整個打開 , 如果我直接把它打開 , 我們在萬神廟的正面向下看 , 我們在看的是正方形 , 或多或少 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把書換一下 , 我們就在廣場上看到萬神殿的正面 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有把戲--只是一本沒打開的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這看起來很可行 。 我心想 , 也許我會把它內部做出來 , 甚至可以把摺疊和全部部分開放的書結合 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以我們進入了萬神殿內部 , 它就成長了 , 諸如此類 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我想 , 也許我是在正確的軌道上 , 但它似乎失去了它的人類特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想讓大家注意一本書 , 一路收集資訊 , 這點總是件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 擊敗了我 , 稱之為 「 趕流行 」 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果是寄來的鴿子會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德修斯 」
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果標題行得通 , 用它吧 。 但它會是穿越羅馬的旅程 , 展示所有我喜歡的羅馬 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	坐落在教堂頂樓的鴿子
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天飛走 , 做成一般鴿子的事 。 再回來 , 整個地方都被鷹架和綠色的網子遮住了 , 沒有這種鴿子可以回家了 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以這是一隻無家可歸的鴿子 , 它將必須再找一個居住地 , 這讓我得以從我喜歡的事物的目錄來看待 , 我們從最高的那一群開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許牠必須回去和家族成員一起生活 ; 那並不總是件好事 , 但牠確實會讓鴿子們再次聚在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我想 , 這有點意思 , 但或許有一個人應該用某種方式來參與這件事 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙 , 一輩子都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到任何地方 , 去找他們危險的地方 , 那些他們和這個傢伙變成朋友 , 並且在午餐時間學會欺騙他和娛樂他 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	還有一個真正的鍵結在這個老男人和這些鴿子之間發展出一個真正的鍵結
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 在故事的結尾 , 他真的病得很重 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教他們拼他的名字aldo
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們一天又三、四天沒見到他──他住在一個小閣樓裡──他們會拼出他的名字然後飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於有了充足的力量 , 爬上梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 一顆紅色的氣球 , 都在那兒等著他 , 然後他們把他載到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這一點:每當他失去一隻鴿子的時候 , 他都會把鴿子帶到城墻外面去 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在羅馬的舊習俗中 , 死者從來不埋在牆內 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這真是個高興的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會走很長的路
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	不管怎樣 , 我還是...如果包裝不行 , 故事也不行 , 我只能想出標題 , 希望書名能正確地把我踢下去 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時 , 它的確會把我弄得夠重 , 我甚至會寫個標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些全部都是標題的最終引領我找到解決方案 , 這是一位年輕女子的故事 , 她在一隻寄來信給羅馬城牆外 , 住在城市裡的某人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	而鴿子正以比亞式飛向下 ,
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墳墓和松果之類的東西 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看這條紅線 , 你看到鴿子的小徑 ; 如果你看不到紅線 , 你就是那隻鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	此時此刻 , 飛越城市的感覺 , 是必要的且可能的 , 試著傳達出那種飛越城市的感覺 , 而非實際行動的感覺 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過了賽斯提烏斯金字塔--這些對你來說應該很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬渡河大門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的事情 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這只鴿子做了一件大部份鴿子不會做的事:它走上一條斯基的路線 。 這個裝置是我覺得有必要真正延長這本書超越四頁的範圍 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們繞過羅馬競技場 , 穿過聖塔瑪利亞的教堂 , 和海克力士走向河流的神殿 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們差點撞上了由米開朗基羅設計的帕拉索法恩斯這塊玉米田 , 用羅馬競技場拿來的石頭建成的 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯瞰campode的光纖
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給學生看的其中一件事因為這是完全的荒誕地 , 完全否定了觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的透視法就是只要看上去可信 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著弄清楚這裡的消失點 ; 有一對在火星上 , 還有另外幾位在克雷莫納州 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但進入廣場 , 就在聖母堂前面 , 一場足球賽無時無刻都在進行中 , 我們被足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	現在這張關於被足球擊中的糟糕的插圖
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的作品 。 聖母塔瑪麗亞•德拉的步調 , 有足球 , 有一點鳥的翅膀沒什麼變化 , 所以我必須重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你真的想看清楚santamariadella的步調這些書很有彈性 , 令人難以置信的互動性只要轉過頭然後從另一個角度看它就行了
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	穿過巷子 , 我們能看到撞擊的效果是用紅線捕捉的 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	然後鳥類設法把自己從中世紀的塔樓上拉到中世紀的塔樓上--少數幾個中世紀的塔樓通向santagnese教堂還有在下面的圓頂望向下看進了廣場大的navona我們已經看到、飛過好幾次了還有四條河流的貝尼雕像--然後再過來是美妙的布羅米尼聖依華教堂在26英尺的距離足夠長 , 停下了通往上游
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	接著 , 我們在內部和四處飛行 , 因為我們在飛行中 , 我們不用擔心重力 , 在這個特定的時段 , 這幅圖可以追溯到頁面的任何方向 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	我們通過gesu會變得很開心 ; 用這種方式來模仿建築並不讓人意外 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	穿過一堵牆 , 充斥著我剛剛講到的那種美麗雕刻 ; 漂亮的雕刻在霓虹的 「 暴風雨 」 上方的牆 , 諸如此類 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後我們到了palazzo的前庭也就是我們的目的地
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓 , 在那裡有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他把鳥兒腿上的訊息給除去了 ; 這是他說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	看著那幅畫板 , 我們看到他正在做的 , 事實上 , 是鴿子所拍攝的旅程的地圖 , 紅線劃過所有視野 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這個資訊 , 這樣我們就完成了這個理解的循環 , 你只需要讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的天際兔子研究了自組裝的概念 , 認為與其建構出某種東西 , 我們還能創造出一種材料來建造自己 , 很可能就是一股dna緊密結合在一起 。 這是在早期階段的一個大概念 ; 兔子展示了三個可以暗示未來自組裝的三項目 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天文台:我們能不能做出能自己做的東西 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想要向各位展示我們未來製造東西的方式 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 我們的建築物和機器將很快便能自組 , 複製和修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我要給你們看 , 我相信是當前的製造業狀態 , 然後比較一些自然系統 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在當前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓--兩年半的時間 , 五十萬至一百萬個部分 , 相當複雜 , 令人興奮的新技術在鋼鐵、水泥、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人振奮的機器 , 能帶我們進入太空五年--250萬個部件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有大約兩百萬種蛋白質 , 可以在一萬納秒折疊 , 或是dna有三十億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一小時複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統有這麼複雜 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠遠超過任何我們能建造的東西 , 遠遠超過任何我們能建造的東西 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們在能源方面更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且他們可以修復自己長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以關於自然系統 , 有一些超級有趣的事情 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能將這些轉化為我們的建築環境 , 那麼我們建造東西的方式就有一些令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想利用我們的物理環境中的自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想建設的複雜性所以我們的建築物和機器
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列──基本上是我們的建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的部分 , 可以用這個序列來折疊 , 或是重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能源將允許它啟動 , 讓我們的部件能夠從程式中摺疊起來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的修正冗餘 , 來保證我們已經成功地構建我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要向各位展示一些項目 , 是我和我在麻省理工學院的同事正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩名是macrobot和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些項目都是大規模的可重構機器人--8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們嵌入機械電裝置 , 傳感器
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你解碼什麼便折疊成什麼 , 成序列的角度--負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120--類似的東西 , 這樣的角度 , 或輪流順序 , 你便發送通過弦序列 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都帶著它的訊息──負120──它會旋轉 , 檢查它是否到那裡 , 然後把它傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些都是傑出的科學家、工程師、設計師在這個專案上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我想這真的可以帶來光明:這真的可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 大量的男人小時來製造這8英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們可以擴大規模嗎 ? 我們能否真正嵌入機器人的每一個部分 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 並著眼於被動的本質 , 或是被動地試圖重新配置可編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 它嘗試有實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上是最基本的計算機建構 , 數位邏輯閘 , 直接嵌入到你的零件裡 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是nandgate
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個正四面體 , 也就是門 , 會做你的計算 , 你有兩個會輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中之一是來自用戶的輸入 , 如同你在造你的磚塊一般 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一塊是從之前放置的磚
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它給你3d空間的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以這意味著 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要的磚頭上插上線 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算著它之前做什麼 , 你說你想要它做什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間裡移動--向上或向下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , [1 , 1]輸入等於輸出0 , 它便下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入是1輸出 , 它會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	那真正的意思是我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的東西的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有了所有內建的信息 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	所以這代表我們可以有某種形式的自我複製
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自我引導的複製 , 因為你的結構包含着確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以換一個零件 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有局部嵌入的信息會告訴你如何修復它
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以 , 你可以擁有爬上去的東西 , 讀完後 , 一對一輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有任何外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個項目叫做偏置鏈 , 它可能是我們現在被動自組裝系統最令人興奮的例子 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它將可重組與可程式化的系統變成完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你是有一個元素鏈 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素是完全相同的 , 它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每個鏈 , 或每個元素 , 都想向右或向左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈 , 你基本上是在編程 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你是在告訴每個單位是否應該向右轉或者向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	當你搖動鏈條 , 它便會折疊成你編程的任何組態 , 在這個例子中 , 一個螺旋形 , 或在這個例子中 , 兩個彼此相鄰的立方體 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上你可以將任何立體的形狀或一維的二維空間編碼 , 完全處於被動地進入這條鏈中 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們什麼關於未來 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為這告訴我們 , 自組裝、複製、修復身體結構、建築、機器有新的可能性 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些部份有新的可編程 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	而從那你就有新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物 , 橋樑 , 機器 , 我們所有的磚其實可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是驚人的並行和分佈式的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以對此是令人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為 , 我在此展示的這些項目只是對於這個未來的一小步 , 如果我們實施這些新技術來做一個新的自組裝世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們已經登上了月球 , 繪製出各大陸的地圖 , 我們甚至去過海底兩次最深的地點 。 是什麼為了探索而離開的下一代 ? 生物學家和探險家nathanwolfe提出了這個答案:幾乎所有事情都能開始 。 而我們能開始 , 他說 , 對於那些不可思議的微小世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索性、微生物學、科學
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolfe:探索剩下的是什麼 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡向一位偉大的20世紀探險家roychapmanandrews致敬
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他任職於美國自然歷史博物館的期間 , andrews引領了一系列的探險活動範圍不明 , 像是在戈壁沙漠這裡 。
he was quite a figure .	他相當是一個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	據說是之後印第安納瓊斯角色的基礎
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我對一群中學學生發表了一段公開的演說 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在這裡要告訴大家 , 如果有任何事比在ted這裡演講還要嚇人 , 那就是試著要把一群12歲小伙子的注意力放在45分鐘的講座上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在演說結束時 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但自此之後 , 有一個問題深深吸引了我 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們應該要去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為我們很多人都有一種感覺就是地球上偉大的探索年代已經結束了對於下一代來說他們將必須去外太空或深海處尋找一些重要的探索事物
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上無處可尋 , 無處可尋嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想生物學歷史中我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未知世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck ,
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	beijerinck一開始要找出菸草鑲嵌病的起因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他做的是從菸草植物中取出被感染的汁液 , 然後用愈來愈小的過濾器過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他達到了當時他認為一定有比當時已知的最微小生命形式還要小的東西 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘經紀人命名 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 拉丁文
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭露病毒的過程中 , beijerinck為我們開啟了一個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒構成地球上絕大部分的基因信息 , 比起所有其他形式的生命體的基因信息加起來還要多 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	顯然已經有大量的實務應用和這個世界有關 , 例如天花的消滅 , 疫苗對抗子宮頸癌的出現 , 我們現在知道大多數由人類乳突病毒所引起 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現不是500年前發生的事情 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約在一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上我們有汽車 , 但卻不知道組成我們星球上大多數基因信息的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有了這些了不起的工具可以讓我們探索未知的世界--像是深度定序 , 讓我們可以做得不僅僅是跳過表面 , 還能觀察特定物種的個別基因組 , 還可以觀察整個公尺見解 , 我們身邊充滿了微生物的社群 , 並且紀錄這些物種中所有的基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技術應用到從土壤到皮膚 , 以及中間的一切 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織裡 , 我們現在定期在做這件事 , 找出造成疾病爆發的原因 , 都是不清楚的 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓大家了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們取了你們每一個人的鼻腔標本 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們通常會去找呼吸道融合瘤 , 如流感 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到非常大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究遺傳信息 , 我們會看到一些普通的可疑物--當然 , 很多的人類基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大部分都來自你鼻子內完全無害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到非常非常令人驚訝的現象 。
