as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始檢視這些資訊時 , 我們會看到你鼻子中大約百分之二十的基因信息不符合任何我們以前曾經見過的東西--沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們還不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些實際在研究這種資料的小團體 , 其實我們當中少數人已經開始稱這個資訊為生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是任何以前我們看過的東西 ; 它有點像是一個在我們基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻腔中百分之二十的基因信息是很多的生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸道 , 高達百分之四十或五十的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使是在相對比較下無菌的血液中 , 大約百分之一到二的信息是暗物質無法被分類 , 也不能和我們以前看過的任何東西匹配 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們覺得這也許是手工藝品
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得愈來愈準確 , 我們已經確定這些信息是一種生命型態 , 或至少其中一部分是有生命的 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設都只是在其嬰兒期 , 但仍有令人非常非常興奮的可能性存在:那埋藏在生命中的 , 在遺傳信息中 , 是尚未被辨識出的生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一連串的a、t、c和g , 我們可能會發現一個全新的生命階段 , 就像beijerinck , 它會從根本上改變我們對生物本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這也許可以讓我們找出折磨人類的癌症病源 , 或辨識出我們不熟悉的爆發病症原因 , 或也許創造出分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣布 , 同時也與斯坦福大學、加州理工學院和加州大學舊金山分校的同事一起 , 我們現在正要開始探索生物暗物質 , 探索新的生命形式的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們不知道病毒 , 一種組成我們星球上大多數基因信息的生命形式的生命 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能驚嘆 , 我們可能完全沒有意識到眼前的新生命種類 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能記錄了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能也發現了所有的哺乳類動物 , 但這不代表地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同伴提供了一個重要的課題給下一代的探險家就像來自威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市的年輕女孩一樣
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想 , 如果我們要說出這個教訓的話 , 那就是像這樣的:不要假設我們目前認為有的就是完整的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	追求任何你選擇要探索的領域中的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊到處都有未知的事物 , 它們正在等待被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳說性科學家大衛.迪普希在後面放了理論物理 , 來討論更急迫的問題:我們人類的生存 。 第一步邁向解決全球暖化 , 他說 , 就是承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	在宇宙的位置上daviddeutsch 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出一個肢體外說些令人驚訝的話
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以我會試著這麼做 , 但我想先從大家都知道的兩件事說起 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	而第一個 , 事實上 , 是有史以來最為人所知的東西 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境等等 , 都獨一無二地適合維持我們的演化或創造 , 正如它過去的思維、現在的存在 , 最重要的是我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	今天這個想法有個戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	有個想法是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是充滿敵意的 , 內部是我們僅有的 , 我們賴以為生的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一次機會:如果搞砸我們的太空船 , 我們沒有其他地方可以去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	現在 , 第二件大家都已經知道的事 , 與大部分人類史上所相信的相反 , 事實上 , 人類並不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬霍金說過的 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面的化學汙垢而已 , 它就在一個典型的恆星旁邊 , 它位在一個典型的銀河系的郊區 , 以此類推 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	現在 , 大家都知道的第一件事 , 有點像是說我們處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨特適合...等等 。 第二件事是說我們處在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其當你把這兩個當作生命中深刻的真理並以此作為你人生決策的依據 , 那麼他們似乎彼此有些衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止兩者都是完全錯誤的 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 讓我從第二個開始:典型的地方開始 。 嗯 , 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 讓我們環顧四周 , 然後從隨機的方向看 , 我們看到一個牆 , 還有一個化學污垢 , 這完全不是宇宙的典型 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只需要朝著同一個方向前進幾百英里 , 然後往回看 , 你不會看見任何牆壁或化學污垢 , 你只會看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你往遠處看 , 你會看到太陽、太陽系、恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但那仍然不算典型的宇宙 , 因為恆星在星系中來來去去去去去去 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	在宇宙中的大部分地方 , 宇宙中一個典型的地方 , 離任何銀河系都很近 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們更進一步 , 直到我們走出銀河 , 再回頭看 , 是的 , 巨大的星系 , 帶有螺旋手臂 , 擺在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時我們已經走了十萬光年
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但是我們還沒有接近宇宙中一個典型的地方.
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 你要到達一個星系間空間的1000倍之多 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中一個典型的地方長什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	以極高的代價來說 , ted已經安排了一種高解析度的實境虛擬實境 , 一種星系間空間的景觀 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	請把燈關掉 , 看得見嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美 , 你看到在星系間的空間中 , 完全漆黑一片漆黑 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它是如此的黑暗 , 如果你正看著離你最近的恆星 , 而那顆恆星正如超新星般爆炸 , 當光線抵達你時 , 你甚至會直接盯著它看 , 即使只是閃爍的光芒 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙就是如此的巨大和黑暗
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星很明亮 , 一件非常聰明的事件 , 它會讓你在幾光年內結石死亡 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而在星系間的空間 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你甚至看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡也非常寒冷絕對零度不到三度
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	而且它很空 , 真空的密度比目前地球上最好的科技所能創造出的真空密度要小一百萬倍因此 , 地球上最好的一個地方就這麼不同了
and that is how untypical this place is .	這地方就是如此的不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	拜託 , 我們能開燈嗎 ? 謝謝大家 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們怎麼知道這麼遠的一個環境 , 如此不同 , 如此不同 , 如此不同於我們習慣的任何事物 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式存在--創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這是什麼意思呢 ? 嗯 , 看得更遠從這裡開始 , 我是指望遠鏡你會看到類似恆星的東西
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 類星體 」 。 原本的 「 類星體 」 原本是 「 類星體 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著看上去有點像恆星的東西 。 但它們不是恆星
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	而我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億年前 , 甚至數十億光年之外 , 一個星系中心的物質朝著超大質量的黑洞傾斜 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後密集的磁場引導出重力塌陷的一些能量 。 其中的一些物質 , 以巨大的噴流的形式回到外面 , 照亮了大葉 , 而有著萬億個太陽的亮光 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人類大腦的物理學與這樣一個噴射流的物理幾乎不同 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法在其中一個噴射流中存活下來 。 語言在描述噴射流中會是什麼樣子 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這就有點像經歷一次超新星爆炸 , 但在點的範圍內還要再往上數百萬年 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這個噴射流發生得如此地精確 , 以至於數十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 模型 , 和預測 , 及解釋 , 最重要的是 , 有個參考資料在那裡發生了什麼事 , 在現實中 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另一個 「 夸拉 」 的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不單只是一個表面的圖像 , 雖然它包含了這張圖 , 也包含了解釋性的模型 , 具體呈現出相同的數學關係以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 , 如果這還不夠驚人 , 對另一種結構的信心會隨著時間增加 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特殊的性質 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	實體的物體 , 不像它們可能的樣子 , 除非它們能夠體現出相同的數學和因果結構 , 且隨著時間不斷地表現得越來越多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以我們是一個不一樣的化學污垢 。 這個化學污垢具有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含不斷的精準 , 所有東西的結構 。 這個地方 , 和宇宙中其他地方 , 是一個包含一切結構和因果關係的樞紐 , 包含整個實體現實的結構和因果關係 。 因此 , 物理定律在這裡是最不重要的 , 甚至是強制性的 , 它是物質世界最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	現在太陽系和我們的環境又是如何以我們自身的形式在與宇宙的其他部分取得這種特殊的關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	關於史蒂芬霍金的評論中 , 有一點是正確的 , 但這是錯誤的強調 。 有一點是正確的 , 是與任何特殊的物理無關的 。 沒有特殊的憑證 , 沒有奇蹟的依據 。 它只靠三件我們擁有的特殊事物 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的一種形式 。 資訊的處理是計算 , 電腦需要的是沒有物質的知識 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體能夠發揮我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三點 , 比較不具體 , 但對於開放式的知識、解釋 , 也是必要的 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境被證據淹沒了 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好可以測試看看牛頓的引力定律大約在300年前
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但是我們過去用的證據是降低在地球上每平方公尺前數十億年的數據 , 之後還會繼續下去 。 所有其他的科學也同樣如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	就我們所知 , 發掘所有科學最基本的真理 , 都在這裡 , 只是為了我們星球上的事情 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的地點充斥著證據 , 還有物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三個開放式知識創造的前提條件 , 已屬於它們的可能性最低 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	就像我說的 , 那裡空無一物 , 寒冷 , 外面一片漆黑 , 還是 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	其實那只是另一個狹隘的錯誤認知 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	想像一個在星系間空間中的立方體 , 大小和我們的房子一樣 , 太陽系 。 現在這個立方體被人類的標準給空了 , 但這仍然意味著這個立方體有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造 , 例如 , 一個自給自足的太空站 , 有一群科學家 , 致力於創造開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在已經遠遠超出當前的技術甚至將從星系間空間收集的氫氣形成其它元素等等
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果有東西不被物理定律所禁止 , 那麼 , 有什麼可能會阻礙我們去做 , 除了知道如何 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是關於知識 , 而不是資源的問題 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們可以自動做到這點 , 就有能源供應 , 因為變通會是核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 還是一樣 , 對人類的感官來說那裡漆黑一片.但是你要做的就是拿一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是現在設計 , 往外看去 , 你會看到和我們從這兒看到一樣的銀河系.
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	再加上一個更強大的望遠鏡 , 你就能看到恆星 , 以及行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將能夠實現天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能最困難的科學是生物學實地考察 , 因為需要花費數百萬年才能到達最近的有生命的星球 , 再回來 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你--對不起richard--但是我從來都不喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每隔幾億年就做一個 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間空間確實包含了開放式的知識創造的前提條件 。 任何這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中的任何地方 , 都可以成為和我們一樣的中心 , 只要我們知道如何實現這些知識的存在 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們不是唯一適宜居住的地方
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間的空間能夠創造出一串開放式的解釋 , 那麼 , 幾乎所有其他的環境都是一樣的 。 那麼地球也是一樣 。 受污染的地球也是一樣 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而限制性因素 , 這裡和這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 但知識 , 很匱乏 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個以宇宙為基礎的知識觀點--也許我認為應該使我們感到十分特殊 。 但同時也應該使我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若沒有特定的知識需要生存於宇宙中不斷地面臨的挑戰 , 我們將無法生存 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	僅僅是幾光年外的一個超新星 , 我們都會死 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	martinrees最近剛寫了一本關於我們人類對於各種事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出錯 , 最重要的是用大規模毀滅性武器來恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機率能在這個世紀存活 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他等會兒再在大會上會談到這點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為這個可能性是正確的分類來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我的確同意他的看法 。 我們能生存下來 , 而且我們無法生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這並不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否能及時創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險完全不是前所未見的.物種隨時都在滅絕.
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終究會結束 。 絕大多數曾經存在過的物種和所有的文明都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外的話 , 邏輯上我們唯一的希望就是利用這個特點來區別我們的物種和文明與其他所有人--也就是我們與物理定律的特殊關係我們的能力創造新的解釋 , 新的知識成為存在的中心
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我把這個應用到當前的一個爭議 , 不是因為我想提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是用來說明我所指的那種解決方案 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而爭議是全球暖化
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	現在 , 我是一個物理學家 , 但是我不是一個正確的物理學家 。 關於全球暖化 , 我只是一個層層層人 。 對於一個層層層次來說 , 理性的事情是認真看待科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太晚了 , 以致於無法避免一場災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為 , 如果目前我們最好的選擇是用一種像是京都議定書之類的 , 來避免二氧化碳排放 , 它的經濟活動限制和它在經濟活動上的巨大成本 , 花費數千億美元之類的 , 那麼 , 這已經是不合理的手段了 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	所提倡的行動 , 甚至沒有為解決問題而爭取 , 僅僅是稍微推遲這個問題 。 所以 , 為了避免它已經太遲了 , 而且從有人意識到危險之前 , 可能已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	可能已經太晚了 , 在1970年代 , 最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放即將降低一個新的冰河時期 , 數十億人將會死亡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這一教訓對我來說再清楚不過了 , 我也不知道為什麼它沒有告發公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們不能一直都知道 。 當我們知道一個即將發生的災難 , 以及如何以一個小於災難本身的成本來解決它 , 那麼就真的不會有太多爭論了 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防原則 , 就可以避免我們尚未預見的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要解決問題的方法 , 而不僅僅是問題本身 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	一盎司的預防等於一盎司的解藥但是這只有我們知道預防什麼的
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你因為鼻子被打了一拳 , 那麼醫學的科學就不會教你如何避開拳頭 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不在研究治癒的方法 , 只專注在預防上 , 那它也幾乎不會達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	此時此刻 , 世界正用計畫來強迫氣體排放不計成本的減少 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該會和計畫配合降低溫度 , 計畫要在更高溫度下生存 , 且不是不計成本 , 而是有效率、便宜地生存 。 還有一些類似的計畫 , 像是在太空中放置鏡子 , 將太陽光反射出去 , 並鼓勵水生生物多吃二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些東西都是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類投入心力去面對這個問題的中心 , 或一般性的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	面對我們尚未意識到的問題 , 放下正確的能力 , 不是無限期的避免的好運 , 是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 更是生存的問題 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩個石板 , 然後在上面刻上雕刻 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一塊刻上 " 問題是可以解決的 "
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一張雕刻上寫著: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果困在不良規則的體制 , 經濟學家保羅•羅默揭露出一個大膽的想法: 「 特區市 」 、 「 城市管理區 」 , 由一個國家聯盟所管理 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	paulromer的激進想法:特區市 。
take a look at this picture .	請看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們留下了一個非常引人入勝的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的街燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我碰過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	例如選一件 , 穿綠色上衣的那件 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也來給他一個名字:nelson 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我敢說尼爾森有支手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	所以這個謎題就是:
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森可以接觸到像手機這樣尖端的科技 , 但是卻無法接觸到一百年來在家裡產生電燈的科技 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡單來說 , 答案就是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不良的規則可以防止雙贏解決方案的出現 , 當人們可以把新技術帶進來 , 讓像尼爾森這樣的人也能使用 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司遵守一條規則 , 說它必須以極低的價格銷售 , 事實上 , 補貼的價格太低 , 以至於它在賣出的每一單位都會損失 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	它既沒有資源 , 也沒有動機去連結許多使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想改變這條規則
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他見識過 , 有可能有不同的規則規則 , 企業賺取小額利潤的規則 , 所以他們有動機去簽更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這就是尼爾森公司購買的手機電信系統的那種規則 , 不受地面操作 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過那些規則是如何運作良好 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變用電價制定的規則 , 但卻引發了企業及消費者的抗議 , 想要保存既有的補助制度 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他被困在規則中 , 避免他讓雙贏解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森被困在街燈下進行研究
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	那時 , 真正的挑戰在於找出我們要如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	是否有一些規則可以用來改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想要說明的是 , 我們能夠實踐一個一般性的抽象洞見 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給予人們更多選擇 , 給那些在很多國家裡 , 領導者更多的選擇 , 他們也是人民 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但是 , 要呈現出這兩者之間的反對意見是很有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想給領導者的那種選擇 , 像是給總統提高電價的選擇 , 帶走經濟所想要的人的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能選擇繼續消耗補貼電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能想辦法給雙方更多的選擇這會給我們一套規則用來改變規則使我們脫離陷阱
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也有網路用 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則的破壞性影響 , 規則能讓人們留在黑暗中 , 看看美國太空總署在夜間拍攝的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看見北韓 , 在這裡和它的鄰近地區比起來就像是個黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會很驚訝地發現北韓的規則讓人們留在黑暗中
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但很重要的是 , 要了解北韓和南韓開始時用的是同一套規則在法律和法規上 , 也要能更深入地了解 , 規範、文化、價值和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做出了選擇 , 導致了非常不同的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	因此 , 我們可以改變人類可以改變彼此互動的規則 , 變好或變壞 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個地區 , 加勒比海
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 放大到這裡
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很暗 , 跟這邊的鄰居相比 , 多明尼加共和國也差不多數量的居民 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家相對於波多黎各來說 , 兩國的狀況都很黑暗 , 這兩個國家的居民佔了海地或多明尼加共和國的一半 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們的是 , 規則可能會有不好的情況 , 因為政府的軟弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不僅僅因為政府實在太強而有壓迫感 , 像北韓的情況一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想要創造出有良好體制的環境 , 我們就不能只是撕下來 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須想辦法建立起來 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國戲劇性地展現出與規則合作的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回顧這張圖表的一開始 , 中國曾是世界高科技領導者 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人有先驅科技 , 像是鋼、印刷、火藥 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從未採用 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則 , 來鼓勵這些想法的傳播 , 一個利潤的動機 , 可以促使這個觀念的傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了一些規則 , 讓創新慢下來 , 讓中國遠離世界 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界上其他國家的創新 , 在這方面 , 開發出更新的技術 , 同時也發展出更新的規則 , 中國也被這些進步給砍掉了 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	國民所得停滯不前 , 世界其他地方的收入停滯不前 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的資料
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它描繪了中國的平均收入佔美國平均收入的百分比
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50、60年代 , 你可以看到這個數字大約是3% 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但到了70年代末期 , 情況改變了
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國開始發展 , 中國開始趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你在夜晚回到地圖上 , 你可以得到一個線索引領中國發生劇烈變化 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的點就是你們在輪廓邊上看到的這裡是香港
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港本來是中國的一小部分在20世紀大部分的時候都是遵循一套很不一樣的體制在運作與中國其他地方所複製的中國規則與當時的勞動經濟體制大為相同
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個有上百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大地到大地 , 到從工作開始 , 像是縫衣、做玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了取得收入增加的過程 , 增加技能 , 導致了在那裡的成長非常快速 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港當時也是一個範本 , 像鄧小平這種領導人可以複製的範本當他們決定全面推行市場模式
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫所有中國人立即轉型到市場模式上 , 他們採取的方式是創建某些特區 , 可以做到 , 在某種程度上 , 英國是這樣做的:讓有機會和市場規則的人合作 , 讓想要選擇在其中的人們有機會去上班 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港周圍建了四個很特別的經濟特區:中國人可以來到這個區塊 , 中國人可以來到這個區塊 , 而且城市可以快速成長 ; 還有外國公司可以來到這個區間 , 製造出一些東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	在香港旁邊的一個地方有一個城市叫深圳
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市中 , 有個台灣公司 , 在座很多人製作了iphone , 他們製作了從中國人到深圳的勞動 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以在四個特區之後 , 有14個沿海城市在同一個層面上開啟了 , 最後在這些人們可以選擇的地點展現出成功 , 他們聚在一起 , 是因為他們提供的優勢 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	證實了成功 , 導致了一致的共識 , 要轉移到整個經濟體的市場模式 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在的中國例子顯示了好幾點
one is: preserve choices for people .	其一是:保存人民選擇的權利
two: operate on the right scale .	二:運作在對的尺度上
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你嘗試改變一個村落裡的規則 , 你可以這麼做 , 但是村落會變得太小 , 以至於得到好處 , 只要有數百萬人在好的規則下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太過龐大 ,
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變這個國家的規則 , 你不能給某些人一個機會 , 看看事情的結果如何 , 然後讓他人放大 , 嘗試新規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你這個機會 , 可以創造新地方 , 只要有新的規則 , 大家都可以選擇 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們夠大 , 能取得當數百萬人在有良好規則下一起工作的所有利益 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以提議是我們對所謂 " 特區市 " 概念
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個明確的憲章開始去吸引建造這座城市所需要的所有規則 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們得要吸引投資者 , 他們要建造基礎設施系統、道路、港口、機場、建築物 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引公司的士氣 , 他們會先雇用那些先搬過那兒的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	而且你會需要吸引家家人 , 那些將來會永久居住的居民 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子取得教育 , 得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	隨著那個憲章 , 人們會搬到那裡去 。
the city can be built .	這座城市是可以建造的
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一而再 , 再而三地
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了讓它可行 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些在憲章中被抓走的
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人民的選擇
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這的確建構在模型中 , 如果我們能夠在沒有人居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從不合時宜的領土開始
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以來到新的憲章底下 , 但沒有人是被迫去活在它底下的 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是給領導者的選擇
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們期望的那種領導者的選擇我們需要在國與國之間建立合作的可能性:例如國與國之間的合作、實際上 , 中國和英國之間的合作 , 先建立一點點市場模式 , 然後再擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國不經意地透過它在香港所做的行為 , 減少了世界貧窮所造成的影響 , 比上個世紀所有援助計畫加起來還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們允許這種合作方式再複製一次 , 我們就能讓這類的利益擴展到全世界 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到一種責任的授權 , 一種掌控權從一個國家到另一個國家的授權來監督某些行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	當我說這句話時 , 你們有些人開始想: 「 這是否剛帶回殖民主義 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	它不是 。 但很重要的是 , 要體認當我們開始思考這些事情時所產生的那種情緒 , 可以阻擋我們 , 可以讓我們再拖回去 , 可以阻擋我們 , 關閉我們的能力 , 以及我們對探索新想法的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義不好的地方 , 在我們一些援助計畫中 , 通常還不好的事 , 就是它涉及了強制和優越的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式與選擇有關 , 無論是對領袖 , 還是對那些將住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是強制執行和優越的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何實踐它 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	我們拿一個特別的領袖raulcastro為例 , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定也想過他有機會為古巴做到像鄧小平為中國做到的事但他在古巴島上沒有香港
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過他還是在南方一點點亮點那有著非常特殊的地位
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣周圍有一區 , 在那裡有條約給美國政府負責一塊土地大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚跑去找加拿大總理 , 說: 「 看 , 雅克斯有可怕的公關問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要脫身 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	你為什麼不 , 加拿大 , 接管 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	經營一個特別的行政區
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一座新城市建設在那裡 。
allow many people to come in .	允許許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近能有一個香港
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會保持下去 。 但這條通往我國家的現代經濟和現代世界的大門 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	這個模式還能在哪裡被試驗呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我曾和領導人談過
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	他們之中很多人完全懂得特殊區塊的概念 , 人們可以選擇將其視為一種規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	制定改變規則的規則
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	這是一種創造新規則的方法 , 讓人民在沒有強制的情況下做出民意 , 強制大家的反對者也能夠強迫 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下 , 他們能對長期投資者做出更有保障的承諾 , 像是投資者會來建港口、建造道路的那種 , 在一個新的城市中 , 他們能做出更有保障的承諾 , 只要他們能和一個合夥的國家一起做 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許在某種安排中有點像是信託管理帳戶 , 把土地放在信託管理帳戶裡 , 合夥的國家需要為此負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲有很多的土地可以建設新城市
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我沿著海岸飛行時照的照片
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣一大片延伸出去的土地上有數億人可以居住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們歸納一下並想想 , 不只是一、二個特區市 , 還有數十個城市 , 可以為數億人創造居住地 , 也許未來世紀就有數十億人搬到城市去 , 會有足夠的土地容納他們嗎 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在整個世界裏 , 如果我們在夜晚去看這些燈 , 有一件事是誤導了我們的 , 那就是 , 視覺上說 , 看來 , 世界上大部分的國家已經是用光來建造的 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	讓我來說明為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	把這代表所有的土地
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個方塊代表地球上所有的可耕地
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被城市三十億人所居住的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些點移到這個長方形的底部 , 你可以看到 , 現有的30億城市居民的城市只佔地球上可耕地面積的3% 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想再為十億人建造城市 , 他們會是像這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們將從百分之三的可耕地提升到百分之四
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們將大大地減少人類在地球上的足跡 , 通過建造更多人們可以遷移的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是受良好體制管理的城市 , 他們可以是讓人安全的城市 , 不受犯罪、疾病和不良衛生措施的侵害 , 這樣人們就有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	能取得像電力這種基本公用事業 ,
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要建造第一座特區城市 , 要花什麼代價 , 才能建造更多城市 ?
it would help to have a manual .	有本說明書是有幫助的 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授們可以做的就是寫些細節 , 可能進入這本手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們管理城市 , 走出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者們在野外
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考一些問題 , 比如 , 假設不只加拿大會談和卡斯楚有關的問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西也參一腳、西班牙 , 也許古巴想成為四向關節的合作夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何訂定條約來做這件事 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒有先例可循 , 但可以很容易地解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這件事 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	新加坡和香港才是一開始就有土地價值的城市 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用土地的價值來支付像警察、法庭等費用 , 但學校體制和健康照護體制 , 讓這個地方更吸引人 , 讓這個地方的居民能有更高的收入 , 如此一來 , 土地就更有價值了 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 提供給建構這區的人的誘因並建立起這區並制定基本規則並往對的方向努力
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有其他很多像這樣的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們如何能有低成本的建築物 , 給第一份工作的人買得起 , 像iphone一樣 , 卻能讓那些建築物更有效率 , 並且確保它們是安全的 , 不會因為地震或是颶風而倒下 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術細節尚待發揮 , 但是我們這些已經開始追求這些事的人 , 已經可以知道 , 沒有道路 , 沒有阻礙 , 除了一個失敗的想像力之外 , 還會讓我們無法實現真正的全球性的雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片做個總結
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以如此幸福 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為思想的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現想法時 , 他們也會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有物品 , 分享代表我們每人都變少了 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那樣的方式來思考想法 , 我們通常會用科技來思考 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有其他類型的想法:規則規則規則 , 規則規則規則規則規則像是 , 咱們來訂個賦予研究大學 , 免費提供某種知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一個體制 , 在那裡我們擁有擁有土地 , 在政府辦公室裡登記的土地 , 人民可以把這些土地宣佈為 「 附屬品 」 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能不斷在有規則的空間上創新 , 特別是在我們想出規則來改變規則的情況下 , 我們就不會卡在不良的規則上 , 那麼我們就能不斷進步真正地讓世界變得更好 , 讓像尼爾森和他的朋友一樣的人不再需要在街燈下學習了 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因組學先驅克萊格•凡特仰賴他的史詩般的遠征隊 , 來談談他的團隊到目前為止 , 發現了數百萬個基因 , 來繪製海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、基因、發明、海洋、科學、科技、
craig venter on dna and the sea	craigventer在dna和海上
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	演講結束後 , 我被幾個人問到我對於老化辯論的看法 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將是我對它唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我明白樂觀主義者比悲觀者要活得更久 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在這18分鐘內我將告訴你們的是 , 我們將如何從讀取基因編碼轉換到開始自己編寫基因編碼的第一個階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅是10年前的這個月我們才出版第一批免費增生有機體的序列也就是流感病毒
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫花了13年到4個月的時間 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在2-8小時內完成相同的基因組計畫
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去的十年裡 , 大量的基因組被加上了:大部份的人類病原體、幾種植物、幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳類的基因組 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	從十多年前開始 , 基因組學在今年底 , 我們可能有三到五組基因組測序 , 大約是幾百組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們在今年剛剛從戈登和貝蒂•摩爾基金會得到了一個資格 , 用來定序130組基因組 , 作為對環境有機體的副作用項目 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們去看 , 外面有什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有把地表上的物體劃在這個星球上 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大多數人不會意識到它 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物構成了地球一半的生物量 , 而所有的動物只佔了所有生物總量的1/3 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許這是牛津人不太常做的事情 , 但如果你曾親身到海邊 , 吞一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升的海水中都有大約一百萬個細菌和一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	少於5 , 000種微生物物種被特徵為兩年前的特徵 , 因此我們決定採取行動 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了第二次的srcer遠征 , 我們在那裡進行了很棒的海洋考察 , 嘗試每兩百英里對海洋進行一次採樣 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始做測試計畫 , 接著移居到哈利法克斯 , 在美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿過加拉巴哥群島 , 橫越太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫越印度洋 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的任務 ; 我們在帆船上進行此項任務 , 有部分能協助鼓勵年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只採集海水並過濾它 , 然後在不同的濾器上搜集不同大小的生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們每24小時可以對一億個字母的基因編碼進行測序 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	通過這樣做 , 我們有了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉個例子 , 當時認為我們眼中的視覺色素在環境中只有一兩種有機體擁有相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 世界上幾乎所有海上生物 , 在溫暖的部分 , 都有這些相同的光感接收器 , 並將陽光當作它們能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地方 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了一百三十萬種新基因和多達五萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在已經將這個計畫延伸到空中 , 藉由sloan基金會的資助 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在測量有多少病毒和細菌我們所有人每天都在呼吸 , 特別是在飛機上或密閉的會堂裡 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的儀器過濾 ; 我們僅僅一天內就收集到十億微生物的數量 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	目前我們正在對這些數據進行排序 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	在收集資料方面 , 我們正在通過加拉巴哥群島 , 我們發現幾乎每兩百英里 , 我們在海裡的樣本中就可以看到極大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	其中的一些邏輯就不同溫度差異來說是合理的
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	所以這是一張衛星照片 , 基於溫度--紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現溫暖樣本與冰冷的水取樣有著極大的差異 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件讓我們相當驚訝的是這些感光受體會探測不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據胺基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些不同區域的變化很大 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外地 , 在深海中 , 大部分是藍色的 , 感光受體通常會看見藍色的光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有大量葉綠素時 , 它們會看見很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們的變化更大 , 可能在極端的情況下 , 朝紅外線和紫外線前進 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了評估我們的基因庫的量 , 我們組裝了所有資料 , 包括所有我們遠離考察的資料 , 其中有超過一半的基因資料 , 總計大約有2千9百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些放進基因家族看看這些發現是什麽:我們是發現已知家庭的新成員嗎 ? 還是我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果我們有大約五萬個主要的基因族群 , 但是我們在環境中採集的每一個新樣本 , 都會針對這些新族群加以排列 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以我們正處於最早階段發現基礎基因、組成物及生命在這星球上
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看到所謂的演化樹 , 我們就在右上角 , 和動物在右上角 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在這大約2千9百萬個基因中 , 我們的基因組只有大約2萬4千種 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有動物放在一起看 , 我們的基因族群大概不到三萬個 , 大概只有十幾種或更多的基因族群 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認為 , 這些基因現在不僅是演化的設計要素 ,
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	而我們以基因為中心的觀點來看 , 或許回到了理查•道金斯的想法 , 而不是以基因為中心的觀點來看 , 這是基因組成的不同構造 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力和過去十年或二十年來dna測序的速度差不多 , 已經變得非常快速、便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們對合成基因組的第一個想法是當我們在1995年完成第二組基因組定序 , 來自micplasma的生殖器 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很漂亮的t恤衫上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800對基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只問一個問題 , 如果有某一物種需要800 , 另一個500 , 那是否有一組基因比較小 , 可能構成最小的作業系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始進行轉位子突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉位子只是隨機插入基因編碼的小段的dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	而如果他們插入基因的中間 , 干擾它的功能 ,
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張所有能接受轉位子插入的基因的地圖 , 我們稱之為 「 非必要基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但結果發現環境對此是非常關鍵的 , 你只能根據環境中的東西來定義一個必要或非必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也嘗試採用更直接的方法 , 研究出13種相關有機體的基因組 , 我們試圖比較所有這些 , 看看它們有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們找到了這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現 , 只有173個基因是共用的13個有機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們不理會其中一種細胞寄生蟲 , 池會稍微擴張一點點 。 當我們觀察核心基因組時 , 它會再擴張 , 大約310組 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因組 , 取決於你在這裡的觀點 , 將近300到400個基因 , 從最小的500個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證實這些想法的唯一方法就是製造一條人造染色體 , 裡面有這些基因 , 我們不得不以一種模塊式的方式來做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 在大型碎片中合成正確的dna是極度困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison , 是我的同事 , 研發出令人振奮的新方法 , 讓我們在兩週內 , 合成一個5000個鹼基對的病毒 , 以100%準確度來看 , 以它的序列和生物學來說 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是一個相當令人振奮的實驗當我們拿了合成dna的片段把它注射在細菌中然後突然之間 , dna開始驅動病毒粒子的生產然後殺死細菌
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一種合成病毒-小兒麻痺病毒-在一年之前被製造出來 , 但只有原病毒1/100的活性病毒且花了三年時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的結構圖
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體能打造自身硬體的例子 , 也是我們用生物學得到的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們立刻轉而關心生物戰 , 我最近在參議院委員會舉行前發表了證詞 , 美國政府設立了一個特別委員會來審查這一區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 很重要的是要讓現實記住 , 對抗人們的想像 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 今天任何已經完成基因組定序的病毒 , 都可以製造出
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們會立刻對伊波拉病毒或天花感到驚恐萬分 , 但這個有機體的dna沒有感染力 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使製造天花的基因組 , dna本身不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正讓國安部門擔憂的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯兩國 , 他們在試圖創造生物武器方面努力 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那些研究真的被終止了 , 在將來 , 製造出設計師病毒的過程中 , 應該會非常少活動 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為 , 在兩年內 , 單細胞生物就有可能
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	有可能在十年內就有這種真核細胞了 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在正在製作數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變放大器和進入這個人工染色體的基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 如何把所有其他人
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一個同源重組系統 , 將這些碎片重新組合成一個染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體衍生出來的 , deinocococcusradiodurans可以帶走三百萬雷得的輻射而且不會被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆發過後它會在12至24小時內重組它的基因 , 在它的染色體被完全拆散後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上無所不在 , 可能現在因為我們在那裡的旅行而在外太空存在 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是由約50萬拉德輻射照射過後的玻璃杯打出的光害 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始發燒且發出啪聲 , 底部的微生物卻變得更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張實際狀況的照片上方顯示的是經過一百七十萬拉德輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體被完全打亂了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	這是24小時後相同的dna自動重新組合 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真的很令人吃驚 , 這些生物能夠做到這件事 , 我們可能有成千上萬 , 甚至上千個地球上有能力做到這一點的物種 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合後 , 第一步就是將它們移植進一個沒有基因組的細胞 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不僅僅是為了瞭解生物學的基礎 , 同時也為了環保及社會問題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們所測序的第三個生物上 , 甲烷janoccusjannaschii , 它生存在沸騰的水溫中 ; 它的能量來源是氫原子 , 它的碳是來自於二氧化碳--它從周圍環境中捕捉回來的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的途徑 , 數千種不同的生物以二氧化碳為生 , 可以把它們捕捉回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其從使用從石油中取得的來進行合成的過程 , 我們有機會使用碳元素並將它從大氣中捕捉回來 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一個有機體住在一氧化碳之外 , 我們用它來當作降低能量來分解水來產生氫氣和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有無數的途徑 , 都是可以用來製造代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦正在和挪威石油公司合作一項重大的計畫要把來自天然氣田的甲烷轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	短時間內 , 我認為將有一個新領域 , 叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有這些新的合成能力 , 這些大量的基因陣列修復以及同源重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 來一天製造一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 正如所有生物學一樣 , 透過篩選來進行篩選 , 不管是對氫化生產做篩選 , 或化學生產 , 或僅是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因所扮演的角色 , 將會很好的接觸到 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們正在嘗試修改光合作用的過程 , 從陽光直接產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節的 , 我們認為有一種氧不敏感的催化酶將會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合細胞酶 , 將複雜糖分解成簡單糖類的酵素 , 並在同一個細胞裡發酵來製造乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	用微生物進行製藥生產已經在各大實驗室中進行了 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物所產生的化學作用 , 是比我們最好的化學家能製造的還要複雜的數量 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來工程的物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能源的來源 , 環境的補救措施 , 也許還能取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我以倫理和政策的研究來作結 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	在1999年 , 我們延遲了實驗的開始 , 直到我們完成了一個一年半的生物倫理審查 , 研究是否應該嘗試製造一個人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與了這個計畫
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	其實這是一個非常奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖都把他們的經文拿來當作法律書 , 卻找不到任何禁止創造生命的理由 , 所以這也沒關係 。 唯一的最終考量是生物戰的面向 , 但給了我們去開始做這些實驗的理由 , 基於我們在做的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	目前史隆基金會剛剛資助一個多機構的研究 , 來找出對社會的風險和益處 , 以及像我自己的科學團隊 , 應該在這個領域中使用的規則 , 我們在向前行時 , 正在嘗試設定好的範例 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了對生物恐怖主義的威脅以外 , 它們是很簡單的議題 , 我們是否能設計東西來產生清潔能源 , 或許能改革開發中國家的做法 , 並透過各種簡單的過程來提供 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普津巴多說 , 快樂和成功來自一個我們大部分人不重視的特性:我們走向過去、現在和未來的方式 。 他建議我們按照時間來校正自己的過失 , 做為改善生活的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心、心理學、科學
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利普•津巴多開出了健康的 「 準時 」 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享關於時間的秘密力量的一些想法 , 在很短的時間內 ,
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	視頻:好的 , 開始計時 , 三十秒的工作室
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 , 安靜下來
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	時間快到了 , 終結排序 , 拿一個
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、7、6、5、4、3、2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利普•津巴多:咱們來看看亞當的誘惑性成就吧 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來吧 , 亞當 , 別那麼不好意思 , 咬一口吧 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 。 別棄伊娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 ,
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 , 一口 。 到底怎麼了 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘惑人的 。 這一切是為了產生、抵抗 , 是的 , 是的 , 不是 , 現在 , 以後 , 衝動 , 反思 , 現在的焦點和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾美德會墮落到當下的熱情
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	那些曾宣誓要在婚前保有性慾和貞潔的少女 。 喬治布希 , 大多數人 , 約有60% , 會在一年內達到性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部份都沒有經由節育 。
so much for promises .	為了承諾太多了 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓tempt4歲的孩子們 , 給他們一個治療方法 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們會有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 那它當然是要付出代價的 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	三分之二的孩子用於誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等 。 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 延後推
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特.米舍爾 , 我在史丹佛的同事 , 在十四年後 , 試圖發現那些孩子有什麼不同 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在很多方面 , 抵制的孩子和被量產的孩子之間存在很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些反抗的孩子sat考試的成績高出250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	那是巨大的 。 那就像一整套不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒被惹上麻煩 , 他們是比較好的學生
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們自信且堅定 。 而對我來說 , 最重要的是 , 他們是 「 未來 」 , 而不是 「 現在式 」 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	觀點的研究是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 將你人類經驗的流動分成時間區或時間類別 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	並且在不知不覺中自動和無意識地這樣做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	文化、國家、個人、社會階級之間 , 不同教育程度的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們會變得偏頗 , 因為你學會了過度使用其中一些而其他的就不太好用 。
what determines any decision you make ?	是什麼決定了你做出的決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要做出一個決定 , 來作為一個行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在當下情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 你感覺如何 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們用那種格式來做決策時──我們稱他們為 「 呈現 」 , 因為他們的焦點就是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在並不重要 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是關於 " 我在過去所經歷的這種情況是怎樣的 ? "
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定基於過去的回憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們要稱這些人為 「 過去式 」 , 因為他們把焦點放在什麼上 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去式 , 也不是現在式 , 只針對未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是關於預期的結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們要稱他們為 「 未來式 」 。 他們的重點在於 「 未來式 」 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	因此 , 時間悖論 , 我想說的是 , 時間觀念的悖論 , 會影響你做出的每一個決定 , 你是完全沒有意識到的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你的視角是有偏見的 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實 , 共有六種方式 , 有兩種方式可以用當下 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以放牧 , 兩種方式成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以注重 " 正面懷舊 " 或 " 負面懷舊 "
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是現代主義的 , 也就是你專注於生活的喜悅 , 或是現在的主義者--這並不重要 , 你的生活已經被控制了 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是 「 未來導向 」 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者你可以是超然的未來:也就是 , 生命在死後就開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展思維的靈活性 , 使得思維觀點能流暢地依情況的需求而變化 , 這才是你要學會的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	很快地 , 最好的時間檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度 " 正面懷舊 " , 適度未來的高度 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	和現代主義的調節 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	而且總是低沉的消極主義和現代主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以最好的臨時混合就是你從過去得到的積極正面能給你紮根 。 你將你的家人、身份和自我連結在一起 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	從未來你能得到的 , 是翅膀能翱翔到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	從現在的享樂主義得到的就是能量 , 能量去探索自己 , 地方 , 人 , 感性 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過度的時光都比正面情緒有更多的負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來為了成功而犧牲了什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	犧牲家庭時間 , 犧牲朋友時間
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	犧牲快樂時光 , 犧牲個人的誘惑力
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了嗜好 。 犧牲了睡眠 。 所以這會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	並且為了工作、成就和控制生活
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我敢肯定 , 和一些ted人產生共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這讓我產生了共鳴 。 我小時候在南布朗克斯區貧民窟長大 , 一個西西里島家庭--所有人都住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我在這裡 , 是個朝前看的人 , 他們因為老師介入而做了這些犧牲 , 讓我有了未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等你要拿到其中兩顆 , 直到我學會了平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了 「 現代主義 」 , 我加上了 「 正面主義 」 的重點 , 所以 , 在76歲 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們正把這點應用在許多世界問題上:改變輟學率、結合癮、增強青少年健康、利用時間隱喻法治癒退伍軍人的創傷後壓力症候群 , 藉著奇蹟 , 提高永續性和保育 , 減少身體復原 , 那裡有50%的退休率 , 改變自殺式恐怖分子的念頭 , 修正家庭衝突的時間範圍 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說 , 生活中的許多謎題都可以透過了解你的時間觀和他人的方式來解答 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 顯而易見 , 但我認為後果真的很深遠 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	百年後有多少頭條會很重要 ? 1000年後 ? kirkcitron的《長遠新聞》專案計畫收集現今不但重要的故事 , 還會在數十年後產生共鳴 。 在ted2010 , 他最近發布的頭條 , 有著塑造我們未來的潛力 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來 , 全球性議題、媒體、新聞、科學 。
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:而現在 , 真正的新聞
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞裡 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	單是路透社一家一年就發佈350萬則新聞
that's just one source .	那只是一個源頭 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:那些故事在長期來看 , 有多少才是重要的 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是 「 長遠新聞 」 背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是長久以來基金會的一個計畫 , 由ted成員凱文凱利和史都華布蘭德共同成立 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的 , 是那些在50、100或10 , 000年後仍然很重要的新聞故事 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過過濾器看新聞時 , 順帶一提 , 很多下跌了 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	以去年最頂級的故事為例 , 這在十年內會很重要嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會很重要嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 還蠻酷的 。
